The Significance of Scholar Biographies in Hanafi Tradition
Biographical account with poem and verification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose of a scholar biography (tarjama) in Hanafi tradition and extract key biographical data from the account of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani.

Core Idea
Biographical accounts preserve the living chain of Hanafi scholarship and inspire devotion to the school.

Biographies of Hanafi scholars are not mere historical records; they function as a link in the chain of transmission (isnad) and as a source of inspiration for students. This lesson examines the biography of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani, the commentator of al-Quduri, to understand how tarajim serve to honor scholars and perpetuate the madhhab's legacy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and author of the biography
Determine who is being described (Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani) and who wrote the account (likely the editor or a contemporary). Note that the passage begins with 'Chapter One: Biography...' indicating a structured biographical work.
2
Analyze the poetic elegy (رثاء)
Read the verses and identify the praises ('courageous, virtuous, noble man', 'great imam', 'a sea whose qualities are lofty') and the lament ('the sciences of Abu Hanifa have died'). Consider how the poem connects the scholar's death to the loss of Hanafi knowledge.
The phrase 'the sciences of Abu Hanifa have died' is metaphorical, emphasizing the scholar's embodiment of the madhhab.
3
Extract the scholar's personal piety
Find the transmitted saying of al-Maydani about death. He asks his loved ones to congratulate him, indicating his hope in Allah's mercy. This reflects the ideal character of a Hanafi scholar: knowledge combined with piety.
4
Understand the verification notes
The editor includes a verification from Sheikh Muhammad Sa'id al-Tantawi about the mosque's name and location. This shows the care for historical accuracy in transmitting biographical details.
Such details strengthen the reliability of the tarjama.
5
Reflect on the purpose of tarajim in Hanafi tradition
Sum up: Biographies serve to document the chain of teachers, authenticate transmitted works, and provide role models. This particular tarjama underscores al-Maydani's stature as a commentator of al-Quduri and his deep connection to Imam Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
وطلب مني ولده أن أنظم له أبياتاً تكتب على القبر، فقلتُ: همام فاضل شهم إمامٌ جليل ذو مقامات شريفة ثوى في رمسه فاعجب لرمس حوى بحراً شمائله منيفة فوا أسفاً قضى عبد الغني سريعاً نحبه ونحـــا(۱) حليفه ربيع الفضل حياً في ربيع بروح وارتياح مستضيفة یکا قد أتى تاريخه زد لقد ماتت علوم أبي حنيفة». اهـ * وقد نقل عن الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني أنه كان يقول: إذا أمسى وسـادي مـن تـرابـي وبـت مجـاور الــرب الــرحيـم فهنــوني أحبائي، وقولوا : لك البشرى قدمت على رحمه الله تعالى رحمة واسعة، وأسكنه فسيح جناته.
*****
سألت.
عن
هذا العلامة الشيخ محمد سعيد الطنطاوي الدمشقي المكي شقيق الشيخ علي الطنطاوي، فأفادني أن جامع الدقاق يسمى جامع القبيبات، وهو في وسط - الميدان، وذلك حين زرته بمكة المكرمة يوم الأربعاء في ٣٠/صفر / ١٤٣٠هـ. (۱) نحا ينحو أي قصد وجاء في المطبوع من علماء دمشق وأعيانها في القرن الثالث عشر الهجري ۷۷۲/۲ : «ونجا حليفه»: بالجيم. (٢) أخذت هذه المعلومة من الإنترنت: حمادة والغنيمي)، وهذان البيتان مکتوبان على قبر الشيخ الميداني، كما حدثني بهذا الأخ الكريم الأستاذ محمد حمادة ابن حفيدة الشيخ الميداني بنت الأستاذ يوسف بن محمد ابن الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني.
Chapter One: Biography of the eminent scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani. His son asked me to compose verses for him to be written on the grave, so I said: A courageous, virtuous, noble man, a great imam with noble stations, he lies in his grave; marvel at a grave that contains a sea whose qualities are lofty. Alas! Abdul Ghani passed away quickly; his companion (or 'his destiny' as per note) the spring of virtue, alive in spring, with soul and delight, a hospitable one. Its date came; add: 'The sciences of Abu Hanifa have died.' End. It was transmitted from Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani that he used to say: 'When evening comes and my pillow is of my dust, and I spend the night neighbor to the Merciful Lord, then congratulate me, my loved ones, and say: Glad tidings to you, you have arrived. May Allah have extensive mercy on him and admit him to His spacious gardens.' ***** I asked about this to the eminent scholar Sheikh Muhammad Sa'id al-Tantawi al-Dimashqi al-Makki, brother of Sheikh 'Ali al-Tantawi, and he informed me that Jami' al-Daqqaq is called Jami' al-Qubaybat, and it is in the middle of al-Maydan. That was when I visited him in Makkah al-Mukarramah on Wednesday 30 Safar 1430 AH. (1) 'Naha' means 'intended'; and in the printed edition of 'Ulama' Dimashq wa A'yaniha fi al-Qarn al-Thalith 'Ashar al-Hijri' 2/772: 'Naja halifuhu' with a jim. (2) I took this information from the internet: Hamadah and al-Ghanimi; and these two verses are written on the grave of Sheikh al-Maydani, as narrated to me by the noble brother Mr. Muhammad Hamadah, grandson of Sheikh al-Maydani (daughter of Mr. Yusuf ibn Muhammad ibn Sheikh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani).
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section (tarjama) on Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani, the author of al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri. The text begins with Chapter One of the biography. It includes a poetic elegy composed for his tombstone, requested by his son. The verses praise the sheikh's virtues and lament his death, metaphorically stating that with him the sciences of Abu Hanifa have died. The sheikh is quoted as having a pious saying about death and seeking congratulations from loved ones. The passage then provides a verification note: the editor asked Sheikh Muhammad Sa'id al-Tantawi about the mosque Jami' al-Daqqaq (also known as Jami' al-Qubaybat), confirming its location in al-Maydan. Finally, a note clarifies a variant reading in the poem and confirms that the two verses are indeed inscribed on the sheikh's grave, as reported by his descendant Muhammad Hamadah.

Key Terms
ترجمة (tarjama): Biographical account of a scholar, often including praise, personal sayings, and verification of details to preserve the chain of transmission.
همام (hammam): A courageous, determined person; used as praise in the poem to highlight the scholar's resolve in serving knowledge.
أبو حنيفة (Abu Hanifa): Imam Abu Hanifa, the eponym of the Hanafi school. Mentioned in the elegy to signify the scholar's connection to the school's founder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a purpose of the tarjama as illustrated in the passage?
A) To honor the scholar's knowledge and piety
B) To provide a legal ruling from the scholar
C) To connect the scholar to the Hanafi tradition
D) To verify historical details about the scholar

Key Takeaway
The biography of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani shows how tarajim preserve the human link to the Hanafi madhhab, combining praise, piety, and verification to sustain the tradition.

The Composition and Merits of Al-Lubab
Describing the merits and composition history of Al-Lubab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the composition timeline of Al-Lubab and explain why it was widely accepted among Hanafi scholars.

Core Idea
Al-Lubab took nine years of meticulous writing and revision, becoming a golden chain connecting earlier and later Hanafi scholarship.

This lesson explores the historical background of Al-Lubab, a celebrated commentary on Mukhtasar Al-Quduri. Understanding its composition period and scholarly reception helps us appreciate the depth and authority of this foundational Hanafi text. We will examine the timeline given by the author himself and the reasons for its widespread acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Identify Merits
Read the first paragraph carefully and list the qualities that made Al-Lubab highly regarded (e.g., containing choicest benefits, linking predecessors and successors, widespread acceptance).
Focus on the phrases 'golden chain' and 'solid ingot' as metaphors for continuity and strength.
2
Extract Key Dates
From the second paragraph, note the three dates: the year Al-Maidani was explaining the Zakat chapter (1261 AH), the first completion (1266 AH), and the final revised completion (1268 AH).
Also note his age at 1261 AH: 39 years.
3
Synthesize the Timeline
Assuming the start in 1259 AH (when he reached the Zakat chapter in 1261 AH after 2 years of work), calculate the total duration from start to final revision: 1259 to 1268 AH = 9 years.
The author suggests the first version in 1266, then revision until 1268.
4
Reflect on Significance
Consider why a nine-year effort and revision process adds to the authority of Al-Lubab. How does this compare to modern expectations of authorship?
This reflects the scholarly rigor of the Hanafi tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن اللباب
جمال جواهر المتأخرين ودررها، كمـا حـوى غُرَرَ الفوائد، وضم شمل كثير من أصول السابقين، وفروع اللاحقين، حتى صار سلسلةً ذهبية متصلة، وسبيكةً متينة غير منفصلة، تُلحق الأحفاد بالأجداد، وتوصل القاصي بالداني. من مزايا اللباب أن العلماء تلقوه بقبول حسن كبير لما وجدوا فيه من مزايا عديدة وهكذا نال اللباب حظاً وافراً مما ناله أصله مختصر القدوري، من البركة والانتشار العظيم بين أهل العلم، وذلك فضل الله يؤتيه من يشاء.

المبحث الثالث
مدة تأليف اللباب
صرح المؤلف الميداني في آخر كتاب الزكاة أنه كان يشرحه سنة ١٢٦١هـ ، أي وله من العمر ٣٩ سنة، وقد انتهى منه مؤلفه سنة
١٢٦٦هـ.
وفي بعض مخطوطات اللباب أنه انتهى منه سنة ١٢٦٨هـ. قلت : ولعله انتهى منه أولاً سنة ١٢٦٦هـ، ثم أعاد النظـر فيـه لتنقيحه وتهذيبه، فكان الانتهاء منه تماماً في المرة الثانية محرراً منقحاً سنة ١٢٦٨هـ، والله أعلم.
وعلى هذا، إذا قدرنا أنه بدأ بتأليفه سنة ١٢٥٩هـ، حيث وصل إلى كتاب الزكاة سنة ١٢٦١هـ، وانتهـى مـنـه محـرراً منقحـاً سـنـة
١٢٦٨هـ، فتكون مدة تأليفه له حوالي تسع سنوات، والله أعلم.
Chapter Two: Study of Al-Lubab. The beauty of the jewels of the later scholars and their pearls, as it contained the choicest benefits, and gathered many principles of the predecessors and branches of the successors, until it became a continuous golden chain, and a solid inextricable ingot, linking grandchildren to grandfathers, and connecting the distant with the near. Among the merits of Al-Lubab is that the scholars received it with great good acceptance because they found in it many merits. Thus Al-Lubab obtained a great share of what its original, Mukhtasar Al-Quduri, obtained of blessing and widespread dissemination among the people of knowledge, and that is the grace of Allah which He gives to whom He wills.

Third Section: Duration of the authorship of Al-Lubab.
The author Al-Maidani stated at the end of the Book of Zakat that he was explaining it in the year 1261 AH, i.e., at the age of 39 years, and he completed it in the year 1266 AH. And in some manuscripts of Al-Lubab it is stated that he completed it in the year 1268 AH. I say: Perhaps he completed it first in 1266 AH, then revised it to refine and polish it, so the completion of the entire revised and refined version was in 1268 AH, and Allah knows best. Based on this, if we assume he began its authorship in 1259 AH, reaching the Book of Zakat in 1261 AH, and finished it revised and refined in 1268 AH, then the duration of its authorship is about nine years, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage introduces the merits and composition history of the book Al-Lubab, a highly respected Hanafi fiqh commentary by Al-Maidani. The author praises the work as a collection of valuable teachings from earlier and later scholars, forming a continuous tradition. He notes that scholars widely accepted it due to its many benefits, similar to the acceptance of its source text, Mukhtasar Al-Quduri. The passage then discusses the timeline of its writing: Al-Maidani stated in the chapter on Zakat that he was explaining it in 1261 AH at age 39, and the first version was completed in 1266 AH. Some manuscripts say 1268 AH. The author suggests that the first version was done in 1266 AH, then he revised it until final completion in 1268 AH. Assuming a start in 1259 AH (when he reached the Zakat chapter in 1261 AH), the total work took about nine years. This biographical insight helps understand the scholarly effort behind this key Hanafi text.

Key Terms
اللباب (Al-Lubab): The title of the commentary by Al-Maidani on Mukhtasar Al-Quduri, meaning 'the core' or 'the essence'.
الميداني (Al-Maidani): The author of Al-Lubab, a Hanafi scholar of the 13th century AH.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar Al-Quduri): The concise fiqh manual by Al-Quduri, which Al-Lubab expounds upon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 1259 AH
B) 1266 AH
C) 1268 AH
D) 1261 AH

Key Takeaway
Al-Lubab took about nine years to compose, including a revision phase, and was widely accepted as a valuable Hanafi text connecting earlier and later scholarship.

Al-Quduri and the Levels of Mujtahids
Colophon, biography, and classification quote

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, state his death date, and explain the first level of mujtahids as described by Ibn al-Kamal.

Core Idea
Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar is a foundational Hanafi text; Ibn al-Kamal's classification shows that the four imams are the highest level of mujtahids.

This passage marks the completion of Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri by Abd al-Fattah al-Maydani. It provides a brief biography of the original matn author, al-Quduri, and begins a quote from Ibn al-Kamal on the seven levels of mujtahids. Understanding this classification helps us appreciate the hierarchy of authority in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work and its completion
Note the book title (Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri), the sharh author (Abd al-Fattah al-Maydani), and the date of completion (Monday, 13 Ramadan 1266 AH).
2
Read the biography of al-Quduri
Find the full name: Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ja'far ibn Hamdan Abu al-Hasan ibn Abi Bakr al-Quduri al-Baghdadi. Note his death year: 428 AH.
He is the author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a widely studied Hanafi text.
3
Recognize the source of the classification
The classification is quoted from a treatise by Ibn al-Kamal, a later Hanafi scholar. This shows the ongoing development of usul al-fiqh.
4
Understand the first level of mujtahids
The highest level are 'mujtahidun fi al-shar'' who independently establish principles of usul and derive rulings, exemplified by the four imams (Abu Hanifa, Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad).
The passage cuts off, but this level is the most independent.

يقول العلامة المحقق احمد المفتى المشهور بابن الكمال التكنه الله مجته في رسالته . اعلم ان الفقهاء على سبع طبقات الأولى طبقات المجتهدين في الشرع كالأئمة الاربعة ومن سلك مسلكهم في تأسيس قواعد الاصول واستنباط احكام
And Allah Most High knows best. It has been completed by the praise of Allah Almighty at the time of the great afternoon of Monday, the thirteenth of the blessed month of Ramadan, in the year 1266 from the Hijrah of the Chosen One described with every attribute, by the hand of its compiler, the humble, hopeful, full of wishes, Abd al-Fattah al-Ghanimi al-Maydani, may Allah forgive him, his parents, his loved ones, and those who have a right upon him, and be good to them and his family. And may He grant us the firm word at the end and on the day of standing before Him. Praise be to Allah who has guided to righteous deeds, and blessings and peace be upon our master Muhammad, his family, companions, and pure wives, eternal blessings and peace as long as times follow one another and vehicles continue. Amen. Owner of the book. The book 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' which was authored by Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ja'far ibn Hamdan Abu al-Hasan ibn Abi Bakr al-Quduri al-Baghdadi, may Allah have mercy on him, ... and he died in Baghdad on Sunday, mid-Rajab, year 428 AH, may Allah grant him vast mercy. Transferred from a collection of biographies. And a statement of the levels of mujtahids and jurists, may Allah sanctify their souls and not make their secrets perish, and may He bestow upon us and upon the Muslims from their blessings. The investigating scholar, the mufti known as Ibn al-Kamal, may Allah give him success, said in his treatise: Know that jurists are of seven levels. The first level is the level of mujtahids in the Shariah, like the four imams and those who follow their path in establishing the principles of usul and deriving rulings.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is a colophon and biographical front matter. It begins with the completion statement of the book 'Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri' by Abd al-Fattah al-Maydani. The author records the exact date of completion: Monday, 13 Ramadan 1266 AH. He includes a prayer for forgiveness and blessings on the Prophet. Then there is a brief biography of the original matn author, al-Quduri (Ahmad ibn Muhammad), noting his lineage and death in 428 AH. Following that, a quote from Ibn al-Kamal explains the seven levels of mujtahids, starting with the 'mujtahidun fi al-shar'' like the four imams who independently derive rulings using usul al-fiqh. This classification is important for understanding the hierarchy of authority in the Hanafi tradition. The text ends abruptly mid-sentence, likely due to a page break.

Key Terms
المجتهد (al-mujtahid): A scholar who derives legal rulings directly from the primary sources (Qur'an and Sunnah) using established principles of usul al-fiqh.
طبقات المجتهدين (tabaqat al-mujtahidin): The classification of mujtahids into levels based on their ability to derive rulings and their reliance on earlier authorities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar is a key Hanafi text, and Ibn al-Kamal's classification reminds us that ijtihad exists at multiple levels.

Understanding the Author's Colophon of Al-Lubab
Author's completion note with date and personal details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author and completion date of Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri from its colophon.

Core Idea
The colophon dates Al-Lubab's completion to Ramadan 1266 AH by Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani.

A colophon is a scribal note at the end of a manuscript, often containing the title, author, date, and place of completion. This lesson analyzes the colophon of Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri, a key Hanafi fiqh commentary. You will learn to extract biographical information and appreciate the humility and piety expressed by classical scholars in such notes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic colophon aloud
Read the Arabic text of the colophon to become familiar with its style and vocabulary. Note the opening phrase 'قال مؤلفه حفظه الله'.
This is a standard opening for a colophon.
2
Identify the author's name and titles
Look for the phrase 'عبد التي النتيسي الميداني' – this is the author. Note the humility expressions 'الحقير الجاني' and the prayer for forgiveness.
The name 'عبد التي' is likely a scribal error for 'عبد الغني' (Abd al-Ghani).
3
Extract the completion date and time
Find the date phrase: 'وقت الضحوة الكبرى من يوم الاثنين ثالث عشر رمضان المبارك سنة ست وستين ومائتين وألف'. This translates to Monday, 13 Ramadan 1266 AH.
1266 AH corresponds to approximately 1850 CE.
4
Note the prayers and blessings
Observe the supplications for forgiveness, for the Prophet ﷺ, and the closing praises. This reflects the author's piety and the tradition of ending books with blessings.
These are standard elements of classical Islamic colophons.
5
Understand the significance
This colophon confirms the author's identity and the completion date, which helps in dating the commentary and understanding its historical context.
This also shows the commentator is not Al-Quduri (the matn author) but al-Maydani.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال مؤلفه حفظه الله : قد تم بحمد الله تعالى وقت الضحوة الكبرى من يوم الاثنين ثالث عشر رمضان المبارك سنة ست وستين ومائتين وألف، من هجرة المصطفى الموصوف بأكمل وصف، على يد جامعه الحقير الجاني، كثير الأماني: عبد التي النتيسي الميداني، غفر الله ولوالديه، وأحبابه ومن له حق عليه، وأحسن إليهم وإليه! وثبتنا بالقول الثابت عند الخاتمة ويوم الوقوف بين يديه! والحمد لله الذي بنعمته تتم الصالحات، وصلى الله على سيدنا محمد وعلى آله وأصحابه وأزواجه الطاهرات، صلاة وسلاماً دائمين ما تعاقبت الأوقات، وتواصلت البركات، آمين.
Its author, may Allah preserve him, said: It has been completed, praise be to Allah Almighty, at the time of forenoon on Monday, 13th of blessed Ramadan, year 1266 AH of the Hijra of the Chosen One, described with the most complete description, by the hand of its compiler, the humble sinful one, of many hopes: Abd al-Ti al-Nutaysi al-Maydani, may Allah forgive him, his parents, his loved ones, and those who have a right over him, and be good to them and to him! And make us firm with the firm word at the end and on the day of standing before Him! And praise be to Allah by whose grace good deeds are completed, and may Allah bless our master Muhammad and his family, companions, and pure wives, a perpetual prayer and peace as long as times alternate and blessings continue, Amin.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This is the colophon of Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri written by the author Abd al-Ghani al-Ghunaymi al-Maydani (d. 1298 AH). He records the completion date as Monday, 13 Ramadan 1266 AH (c. 1850 CE). He refers to himself humbly as 'the compiler, the lowly sinner'. The colophon includes standard prayers for forgiveness and blessings upon the Prophet. This biographical note confirms the author's name and methodology.

Key Terms
الضحوة الكبرى (al-dahwah al-kubra): The forenoon after sunrise, approximately mid-morning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Biography of Imam al-Quduri
Biographical entry of Imam al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical details of Imam al-Quduri, identify his major works, and trace his transmission chain back to the Prophet.

Core Idea
Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar is a foundational Hanafi matn, and its author was a leading tarjih scholar in Baghdad.

This passage presents the biography of Imam al-Quduri, the author of one of the most widely studied primers in Hanafi fiqh. Understanding his life, works, and scholarly lineage helps us appreciate the authority of his Mukhtasar and its place in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and key identifiers
Locate the full name, genealogy, birth year, and epithets (al-Quduri, al-Hanafi, al-Baghdadi). Note the meaning of 'al-Quduri' (seller of pots).
Full name: Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Ja'far ibn Hamdan.
2
Analyze his scholarly rank
Recognize that he was among 'ashab al-tarjih' — scholars qualified to weigh opinions. His leadership in Iraq is emphasized.
He is frequently cited in al-Hidayah and al-Khilaf.
3
List his major works
Identify his authored works: Mukhtasar (al-Quduri), commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi, al-Tajrid, al-Taqrib, and an abridgment for his son.
Al-Tajrid covers disputes between Hanafis and Shafi'is in seven volumes.
4
Note the anecdote about the book's blessing
He carried the Mukhtasar to the Kaaba, hung it from the curtains, and prayed for blessings. The prayer was answered.
The Mukhtasar contains 12,500 issues.
5
Trace the chain of transmission
Follow the isnad from al-Quduri back to the Prophet: from al-Quduri to his teachers up to Imam Muhammad, then Abu Hanifa, then the tabi'un and sahaba.
This chain validates the authenticity of the fiqh transmitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة القدوري رحمه الله تعالى: أحمد بن محمد بن أحمد بن جعفر بن حمدان الفقيه القدوري الحنفي البغدادي صاحب المسمى بالقدوري، ولد سنة اثنتين وستين وثلاثمائة. كان من أصحاب الترجيح، تكرر ذكره في الهداية والخلاف، انتهت إليه رئاسة أصحاب أبي حنيفة بالعراق وارتفع جاهه. صنف وشرح مختصر الكرخي، والتجريد في سبعة أسفار يشمل على مسائل الخلاف بين أصحابنا وأصحاب الشافعي، شرع في إملائه سنة خمس وأربعمائة، وله التقريب في مسائل الخلاف ومختصره جمعه لابنه وغير ذلك. مات في اليوم الخامس عشر من شهر رجب سنة ثمان وعشرين وأربعمائة ببغداد ودفن من يومه في داره ثم نقل إلى تربة في شارع المنصورية. ونسب إلى بيع القدور التي هي جمع قدر. وفي هذه السنة توفي الشيخ الرئيس أبو علي بن سينا كذا في مختصر ربيع الأبرار. وإنه لما صنف هذا الكتاب حمله مع نفسه إلى بيت الله الحرام وعانه من أستاره وسأل الله تعالى أن يبارك له فيه فاستجيب له وجعله مباركاً لذلك. وعدد مسائله اثنا عشر ألف وخمسمائة. اعلم أن أبا الحسن القدوري أخذ الفقه من أبي عبد الله محمد بن الجرجاني عن أبي بكر الرازي عن الحسن الكرخي عن أبي سعيد البردي عن علي الدقاق عن ابن سهل موسى بن نصر الرازي عن محمد بن حسن الشيباني عن أبي حنيفة عن حماد عن إبراهيم النخعي عن علقمة عن عبد الله بن مسعود رضي الله عنه عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم.
Biography of al-Quduri, may Allah have mercy on him: Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Ja'far ibn Hamdan, the jurist al-Quduri al-Hanafi al-Baghdadi, author of the work known as al-Quduri. He was born in the year 362 AH. He was among those who preferred rulings, frequently mentioned in al-Hidayah and al-Khilaf. The leadership of the followers of Abu Hanifa in Iraq culminated in him, and his status rose. He authored and commented on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi, and al-Tajrid in seven volumes covering issues of disagreement between our school and al-Shafi'i's. He began dictating it in the year 405 AH. He also wrote al-Taqrib on disputed matters and its abridgment compiled for his son, among other works. He died on the fifteenth of Rajab, 428 AH in Baghdad and was buried the same day in his house, then transferred to a tomb in al-Mansuriyyah street. He was attributed to selling pots (qudur), the plural of qidr. In that same year, the chief master Abu Ali ibn Sina died, as recorded in Mukhtasar Rabi' al-Abrar. When he authored this book, he carried it with him to the Sacred House of Allah, hung it from its curtains, and asked Allah to bless him in it; his prayer was answered, and it became blessed. The number of its issues is twelve thousand five hundred. Know that Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri took fiqh from Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn al-Jurjani, from Abu Bakr al-Razi, from al-Hasan al-Karkhi, from Abu Sa'id al-Bardi, from Ali al-Daqqaq, from Ibn Sahl Musa ibn Nasr al-Razi, from Muhammad ibn Hasan al-Shaybani, from Abu Hanifa, from Hammad, from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, from Alqamah, from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him, from the Prophet, peace be upon him.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This is a biographical entry about Imam al-Quduri, the author of the famous Mukhtasar (matn) known as 'al-Quduri'. The passage details his lineage, his high status among the Hanafis in Iraq, his major works including a commentary on al-Karkhi's Mukhtasar and 'al-Tajrid' which compares Hanafi and Shafi'i positions. His death date is given as 428 AH, and the text notes that Ibn Sina died the same year. A notable anecdote mentions that al-Quduri brought his book to the Kaaba and prayed for blessings upon it. The later chain of transmission (isnad) connects him back to the Prophet through the Hanafi school, showing his scholarly lineage.

Key Terms
القدوري (al-Quduri): The author of the Mukhtasar (matn) known as al-Quduri, a foundational text in Hanafi fiqh.
أصحاب الترجيح (ashab al-tarjih): Scholars who were qualified to weigh and prefer one opinion over another within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the significance of al-Quduri being among the 'ashab al-tarjih'?
A) He only narrated opinions.
B) He could weigh and prefer one opinion over another.
C) He was a companion of the Prophet.
D) He founded a new school.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Quduri was a leading Hanafi jurist whose Mukhtasar remains a foundational text, validated by his tarjih status and a strong transmission chain.

Parsing Scholar Biographies in Hanafi Texts
Biographical summaries of five Hanafi scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract and interpret key biographical data (name, teachers, works, death date) from a Hanafi scholar biography and relate it to the chain of fiqh transmission.

Core Idea
A scholar's biography is a chain of authority — knowing who taught whom establishes the reliability of legal transmission.

Biographical entries in Hanafi texts are not mere historical data; they are legal evidence. When a fatwa is attributed to a later authority like Ibn Abidin, knowing his teacher's teacher (like Ibrahim al-Sa'ihani) connects the chain back to the founding imams. This lesson trains you to extract that chain from the biographical summaries in Al-Lubab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and laqab
Read the entry carefully and note the ism, nasab, nisbah, and any honorifics (e.g., 'Ibn Rustam', 'Ibn al-Salah').
The nisbah often indicates place of origin (e.g., al-Marwazi from Marw).
2
Determine the scholarly relationship
Identify key phrases like 'student of X' (talmidh) or 'teacher of Y'. This establishes the chain of transmission.
In Hanafi fiqh, direct students of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani hold special authority.
3
List notable works mentioned
Note the titles of books authored. These indicate the scholar's specialty (fiqh, hadith, language).
Works like 'al-Nawadir' are collections of rare transmissions from Imam Muhammad.
4
Record the death date (year AH)
The death date places the scholar in a historical layer, important for evaluating the chronology of legal opinions.
For example, Ibrahim al-Sa'ihani (d. 1197 AH) is a relatively late authority; Ibn Rustam (d. 211 AH) is early.
5
Assess the scholar's role in Hanafi transmission
Consider whether the scholar is a direct transmitter of the founding imams, a commentator, a linguist, or a later jurist. This affects the weight of his narrations or opinions.
Ibn al-Salah is a hadith scholar whose works on mufti adab are cited in Hanafi fatwa methodology.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section from Al-Lubab, listing notable scholars whose works or opinions are cited in the main commentary. The author provides brief details: name, notable works, teachers, students, and death dates. Ibn al-Salah is a famous hadith scholar. Ibn al-Qatta' authored a work on verb forms. This section serves as a reference for the scholarly context of Al-Lubab.

الإمام (al-imam): A title of respect for a leading scholar in a field, here used for Muhammad al-Shaybani and others.

Key Takeaway
Every scholar biography in a Hanafi text is a link in the chain of transmission — identifying the relationship (teacher/student) and death date helps assess the authority of their narrations.

Identifying the Authorities in Al-Lubab's Biographical Appendix
Biographical appendix listing 12 scholars cited in Al-Lubab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each scholar listed in the appendix, classify them as Hanafi or non-Hanafi, and state their key contributions or works relevant to Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Knowing the scholars cited deepens your understanding of the authority chain in Hanafi fiqh.

The biographical appendix in Al-Lubab (the commentary on Al-Quduri) lists 12 notable figures referenced in the commentary. Some are foundational Hanafi jurists whose works form the backbone of the madhhab; others are from complementary disciplines like language, hadith criticism, or other madhhabs. Recognizing who they are and why they are cited helps you appreciate the breadth and depth of Hanafi scholarship and its interaction with other fields.

Guided Path
1
List all 12 scholars
Read through the appendix and write down each scholar's name as given. Note any alternate names or titles (e.g., Ibn al-Humam, Abu al-Barakat).
Include the Arabic names for future reference.
2
Classify by madhhab or field
Based on the descriptions, determine whether each scholar is a Hanafi jurist, a scholar from another madhhab, or a specialist in a non-fiqh discipline (e.g., language, hadith). Look for clues like 'Hanbali', 'muhaddith', or 'language'.
Not all are Hanafi; some are cited for their expertise in language or hadith criticism.
3
Identify major works
For each scholar, note the work(s) mentioned in the appendix. These are often key texts in their field.
Works like Kanz al-Daqa'iq, Fath al-Qadir, and al-Jami' al-Saghir are important in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Assess relevance to Al-Lubab
Consider why each scholar is cited in a Hanafi fiqh commentary. Some are sources of fiqh rulings, others are authorities on language or hadith used in legal argumentation.
Linguists like Ibn al-Sikkit may be cited for word meanings; muhaddithun like Ibn al-Salah for hadith methodology.
5
Trace authority chains (Hanafi only)
For the Hanafi scholars, see if the appendix mentions their teachers or students. This helps you understand the transmission of Hanafi knowledge through generations.
For example, Ibn Rustam was a student of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Chapter Three: A brief biography of the notable figures mentioned in Al-Lubab.
1 - Ibrahim al-Sayahani: He is from the teachers of the teachers of Ibn Abidin, author of Radd al-Muhtar, from the scholars of the 12th century AH. I did not find his biography, and perhaps he is Ibrahim ibn Khalil al-Ghazzi known as al-Salahani or al-Sayahani, d. 1197 AH. See Silk al-Durar 6/1.
2 - Ibn Rustam: Ibrahim ibn Rustam Abu Bakr al-Marwazi, student of Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani. He has al-Nawadir written from his teacher Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, d. 211 AH. Al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 9.
3 - Ibn al-Sikkit: Ya'qub ibn Ishaq, an imam in language and literature, d. 244 AH. He wrote Islah al-Mantiq and Sharh al-Mu'allaqat. Al-A'lam 8/195, Hadiyyat al-'Arifin 2/536.
4 - Ibn al-Salah: Uthman ibn Abd al-Rahman al-Shahrazuri, the jurist and muhaddith imam, d. 643 AH. He wrote Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti, Silah fi Sifat al-Manasik, and 'Ulum al-Hadith. Wafayat al-A'yan 3/243, Hadiyyat al-'Arifin 1/654.
5 - Ibn al-Qatta': Ali ibn Ja'far al-Sa'di al-Siqilli, a master of language, author of Kitab al-Af'al, d. 515 AH. Sir A'lam al-Nubala' 19/433.
6 - Ibn Kamal Pasha: Ahmad ibn Sulayman, Shaykh al-Islam, author of many treatises in Hanafi fiqh, tafsir, hadith, and numerous arts, d. 940 AH. Al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 21, Hadiyyat al-'Arifin 1/141.
7 - Ibn Ma'in: Abu Zakariyya Yahya ibn Ma'in al-Baghdadi, imam of jarh and ta'dil, leader of the preservers, author of al-Jarh wa al-Ta'dil and al-Tarikh fi al-Rijal. He died as a pilgrim in Medina in 233 AH. Hadiyyat al-'Arifin 2/514.
8 - Ibn Malik: Abd al-Latif ibn Abd al-Aziz, known as Ibn Malik, the jurist and usuli, author of Sharh al-Manar and Sharh Mashariq al-Anwar al-Saghani, d. 801 AH. Al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 107.
9 - Ibn al-Humam: Muhammad ibn Abd al-Wahid al-Siwasi, known as Kamal Ibn al-Humam, author of Fath al-Qadir li al-'Ajiz al-Faqir Sharh al-Hidayah, which he did not complete, d. 861 AH. Al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 180.
10 - Ibn Yunus: Ubayd Allah ibn Yunus al-Azji al-Baghdadi, a vizier who was knowledgeable in usul al-din, fiqh, and arithmetic, a Hanbali. He authored Kitab: Awham Abi al-Khattab al-Kalwadhani fi al-Fara'id. Al-A'lam 4/198.
11 - Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi: Abd Allah ibn Ahmad ibn Mahmud Hafiz al-Din, author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, al-Manar, and al-Manafi' Sharh al-Nafi', d. 710 AH. Taj al-Tarajim p. 174, Hadiyyat al-'Arifin 1/464.
12 - Abu Bakr al-Balkhi: Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Abd al-Aziz, known as al-Zahir al-Balkhi, author of a commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir, died in Aleppo in 553 AH. Al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 27, Taj al-Tarajim p. 333, where it says: Abu Bakr ibn Ahmad.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is a biographical appendix by the editor (or commentator) listing the notable figures (a'lam) mentioned in the text of Al-Lubab. It serves as a quick reference for the reader to identify the scholars cited. The list includes a diverse group: Hanafi jurists like Ibrahim al-Sayahani (a teacher of Ibn Abidin's teachers), Ibn Rustam (student of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani), Ibn Kamal Pasha (a prolific Ottoman jurist), Ibn Malik (a Hanafi usuli), Ibn al-Humam (the great Hanafi commentator of al-Hidayah), Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi (author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq and al-Manar), and Abu Bakr al-Balkhi (commentator on al-Jami' al-Saghir). Also included are non-Hanafis: Ibn al-Salah (a Shafi'i muhaddith), Ibn al-Qatta' and Ibn al-Sikkit (linguists), Ibn Ma'in (a hadith critic), and Ibn Yunus (a Hanbali). The biographical data includes death dates and major works. The editor references standard biographical sources such as al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya, Hadiyyat al-'Arifin, and others. This appendix aligns with the pedagogical tradition of introducing key authorities referenced in the main text.

Key Terms
ترجمة (tarjama): A brief biographical entry covering a scholar's name, lineage, date of death, notable works, and sources for further information.
الأعلام (al-a‘lām): Notable figures, specifically scholars and authorities referenced in the book.
اللباب (al-lubāb): The title of the commentary (Sharh al-Quduri) by al-Maydani, meaning 'The Core' or 'The Pith'.

The Biographical Tradition (Tarajim) in Hanafi Fiqh: Scholars of al-Lubab
Biographical notices of scholars referenced in al-Lubab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key scholars cited in al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri and explain the purpose of tarajim in establishing the chain of knowledge in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Biographical notices connect us to the living chain of Hanafi transmission, revealing the human authority behind every ruling.

This lesson examines the biographical notices (tarajim) appended to al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. In the Hanafi tradition, knowing the scholars behind a text is essential for evaluating the weight of rulings. This chapter profiles eighteen jurists, spanning from the 2nd to 10th Islamic centuries, giving us a glimpse into the intellectual genealogy that upholds the school.

Guided Path
1
Understand the role of tarajim in fiqh works
Tarajim provide the chain of authority: who transmitted and authored the rulings you study. They help you assess reliability. This list is from al-Lubab, a commentary on al-Quduri, so it introduces the key figures behind the text.
Even if you don't memorize details, skim for names and dates to sense the scholarly lineage.
2
Scan the list and note the range of centuries
Scholars from 173 AH (Abu 'Isma) to 940 AH (Ibn Kamal Pasha) show the continuity of the Hanafi school over 800 years. Note the geographical spread: Baghdad, Balkh, Bukhara, Aleppo, Egypt, etc.
This illustrates the school's durability and adaptation across eras and regions.
3
Identify one non-Hanafi scholar and reflect
Ibn Yunus (d. after 200 AH) is explicitly listed as Hanbali. His inclusion shows that Hanafi texts sometimes cite non-Hanafi authorities, especially for specialized topics like inheritance.
Always check the madhhab of cited scholars to understand the perspective.
4
Note the criticism of Abu 'Isma and its implications
The text warns that despite his fiqh stature, hadith scholars question Abu 'Isma's narrations. This is a reminder that fiqh authority does not guarantee hadith reliability; jarh wa ta'dil is a separate discipline.
When a ruling relies on a hadith through Abu 'Isma, a mufti may need to consider alternative transmissions.

ابن ملك عبد اللطيف بن عبد العزيز، الشهير بابن ملك، الفقيه الأصولي، له شرح المنار، وشرح مشارق الأنوار للصغاني، ت ٨٠١هـ. الفوائد البهية ص ۱۰۷.

Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section (tarajim) from the book al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. It provides concise notices of eighteen scholars who are cited or referenced in the main text. The author lists each scholar's name, some biographical details, their notable works, and in some cases, their death dates and sources for further reference. The scholars span several centuries, from the 2nd/8th century (e.g., Abu ?Isma, d. 173 AH) to the 10th/16th century (e.g., Ibn Kamal Pasha, d. 940 AH). They include Hanafi jurists, usuli scholars, hadith critics (like Ibn Mu?in), and even a Hanbali scholar (Ibn Yunus). The entry on Abu ?Isma notes that despite his fiqh stature, he is criticized by muhaddithun, which is a point of caution for students relying on hadith transmitted by him. Most entries include references to standard biographical works like al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya (by ?Abd al-Hayy al-Laknawi), Hadiyat al-?Arifin (by Isma?il Pasha al-Baghdadi), and Taj al-Tarajim (by Ibn Qu?lubugha). The purpose of this chapter is to acquaint the reader with the authorities behind the rulings in al-Lubab, fulfilling the tradition of providing tarajim in fiqh works to establish the chain of transmission of knowledge.

Key Terms
الجرح والتعديل (al-jarḥ wa al-taʿdīl): The science of criticizing and validating hadith narrators; Imam Ibn Mu‘in is described as its imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Early Hanafi Scholars in Al-Lubab (Part 1: Scholars 13-18)
Biographical list of six Hanafi scholars from Al-Lubab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify six early Hanafi scholars by their kunya, death date, and major contribution or work.

Core Idea
Knowing each scholar's kunya, death date, and key work anchors the chain of Hanafi transmission.

This lesson covers the first six scholars listed in Al-Lubab's biographical section: from Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani (d. 362 AH) to Abu 'Isma Nuh al-Marwazi (d. 173 AH). These include direct students of Abu Hanifa's companions and authors of foundational texts. Memorizing these names and their roles will help you trace the authority behind rulings in Al-Lubab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the kunya and full name
For each scholar, read the Arabic name carefully. Notice the pattern: 'Abu' followed by an epithet, then the lineage. Write down the kunya as the primary identifier.
The kunya is how scholars are commonly cited.
2
Note the death date and place
Each entry includes a death year (e.g., 362 AH) and sometimes a location. These dates help you place the scholar in the Hanafi chronology.
Death dates are given in Hijri; remember that earlier scholars generally studied closer to the founder.
3
Record the scholar's major contribution
Look for phrases like 'صاحب' (author of) or 'راوية' (narrator of). Identify their famous book or role (e.g., narrator of al-Asl).
Some scholars are known for a single work; others for multiple fields.
4
Check the source citation
Each entry ends with a reference (e.g., الفوائد البهية ص 179). This teaches you how to verify biographical data in standard Hanafi tabaqat works.
You can use these references to look up more details later.
5
Group scholars by generation
Organize the six scholars into rough generations: e.g., early (d. 200s), middle (d. 300s), later (d. 600s). This contextualizes their role in transmitting the school.
Abu Hanifa died in 150 AH, so later scholars are several generations removed.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section from Al-Lubab, listing fourteen Hanafi scholars (numbers 13 to 26) who are cited or referenced in the main text. The author provides each scholar's name, key details such as their teachers, students, famous works, and death dates, along with citations to standard biographical sources like Al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya, Taj al-Tarajim, and others. The list spans from early Hanafi figures such as Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani (d. 362 AH) to later scholars like Abu al-Fadl al-Mawsili (d. 683 AH). Notable entries include Abu Yusuf (d. 182 AH), the famous companion of Abu Hanifa and chief judge, and Abu 'Isma al-Marwazi, who is criticized by hadith scholars despite being a great jurist. The section serves as a handy reference for readers of Al-Lubab to identify the authorities behind the rulings discussed.

Key Terms
أبو جعفر الهندواني (Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani): Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn Muhammad, a famous Hanafi imam from Balkh who died in Bukhara in 362 AH.
المجتبى (al-Mujtaba): A commentary by Abu al-Raja' al-Zahidi on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
كتاب الأصل (Kitab al-Asl): Foundational work of Hanafi fiqh by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, narrated by Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani.
مجمع البحرين (Majma' al-Bahrayn): Fiqh work by Ibn al-Sa'ati (Abu al-'Abbas), covering Hanafi and Shafi'i differences.

Later Hanafi Scholars in Al-Lubab (Part 2: Scholars 19-26)
Biographical list of eight Hanafi scholars from Al-Lubab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify eight later Hanafi scholars by their kunya, death date, and major work or relationship to earlier authorities.

Core Idea
Later scholars build upon the earlier generations; knowing their works connects the historical development of the Hanafi school.

This lesson covers scholars 19 to 26 from the same biographical section: from Abu 'Ali al-Daqqaq al-Razi (d. 3rd century) to Abu Yusuf al-Qadi (d. 182 AH). These include key authors like the author of al-Ikhtiyar, a famous qadi, and a scholar criticised for hadith. Understanding their roles will deepen your appreciation of Al-Lubab's sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the kunya and full name
Read the Arabic carefully; many names include nisbas like al-Razi, al-Balkhi, al-Samarqandi. These indicate geographic origin.
The nisba can help you distinguish between scholars with similar names.
2
Note the death date and century
Death dates range from 173 AH (Abu Yusuf) to 683 AH (Abu al-Fadl al-Mawsili). Group them into early (before 300), middle (300-500), and later (600+).
Abu Yusuf's date is early (182 AH) – he was a direct student of Abu Hanifa.
3
Record the major work or role
Look for titles like 'صاحب كتاب التف في الفتاوى', 'صاحب الاختيار', 'شارح مختصر القدوري'. These works are part of the Hanafi curriculum.
Some scholars are known as teachers (e.g., Abu 'Ali al-Daqqaq al-Razi taught Abu Sa'id al-Barda'i).
4
Check the source citation
Each entry references biographical dictionaries. Learn to cross-reference: Al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya, Taj al-Tarajim, Al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya.
These sources are the standard for Hanafi tabaqat.
5
Connect each scholar to the school's development
Ask: Did this scholar write a commentary? Was he a student of a famous teacher? Did he compile fatwas? This shows how the school evolved through texts and teaching.
For example, Abu Nasr al-Aqta' wrote a commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, a key text.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section from Al-Lubab, listing fourteen Hanafi scholars (numbers 13 to 26) who are cited or referenced in the main text. The author provides each scholar's name, key details such as their teachers, students, famous works, and death dates, along with citations to standard biographical sources like Al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya, Taj al-Tarajim, and others. The list spans from early Hanafi figures such as Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani (d. 362 AH) to later scholars like Abu al-Fadl al-Mawsili (d. 683 AH). Notable entries include Abu Yusuf (d. 182 AH), the famous companion of Abu Hanifa and chief judge, and Abu 'Isma al-Marwazi, who is criticized by hadith scholars despite being a great jurist. The section serves as a handy reference for readers of Al-Lubab to identify the authorities behind the rulings discussed.

Key Terms
أبو يوسف القاضي (Abu Yusuf al-Qadi): Ya'qub ibn Ibrahim al-Ansari, chief judge and prominent student of Abu Hanifa, died 182 AH.
الاختيار (al-Ikhtiyar): A commentary by Abu al-Fadl al-Mawsili on al-Mukhtar, a standard Hanafi fiqh text.
تحفة الفقهاء (Tuhfat al-Fuqaha'): A Hanafi fiqh work by 'Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi (Abu Mansur).
المبسوط (al-Mabsut): A Hanafi furu' work by Abu al-Yusr al-Bazdawi, distinct from the earlier al-Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi.

Identifying Hanafi Scholars and Their Lineages
Biographical list of Hanafi authorities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract key details (name, death date, teacher-student links, works) from a biographical entry in a Hanafi tabaqat work and trace the chain of transmission.

Core Idea
Every Hanafi ruling rests on a chain of scholars; knowing the chain gives the ruling its authority.

The passage you are about to read is a biographical chapter from the commentary al-Lubab. It lists the prominent Hanafi scholars whose names appear in the text, along with their death dates and references to standard biographical dictionaries. This kind of tārikh (history) is essential for a faqīh: it helps you verify the reliability of a transmission, understand the development of the school, and appreciate the personal connections between teachers and students. In this lesson, we will learn how to read such an entry and what each part teaches us about the Hanafi scholarly tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and kunya
Each entry begins with a name (e.g., 'Abu Ali al-Daqqaq al-Razi'). Note the kunya (e.g., Abu Ali) and the nisba (e.g., al-Razi). This gives the scholar's identity and geographical origin.
Multiple scholars may share a nisba; add other identifiers like the father's name.
2
Note the death date (Hijri)
Death dates (e.g., 't 317 AH') help place the scholar in a specific century and establish whether they could have studied with earlier masters.
Exact dates vary between sources; the passage gives one date per scholar.
3
Extract teacher-student relationships
Look for phrases like 'tafaqqaha ʿalā' (studied fiqh under) or 'tilmīdh' (student of). This shows the chain of transmission from earlier authorities.
The chain often connects to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani or directly to Abu Hanifa.
4
List the scholar's known works
Prominent works are mentioned (e.g., 'al-Ikhtiyār Sharḥ al-Mukhtār'). Knowing the work helps you find their legal opinions.
Some entries only mention a commentary or a collection of fatwas.
5
Confirm the source reference
Almost every entry ends with a page reference to a biographical dictionary (e.g., 'al-Fawāʾid al-Bahiyyah p. 116'). This tells you where to find more detailed information.
Common sources in this passage: al-Fawāʾid al-Bahiyyah, Taj al-Tarājim, al-Jawāhir al-Muḍiyyah, Hadiyyat al-ʿĀrifīn.

٣٠ - إسماعيل صاحب شرح الدرر بن عبد الغني النابلسي، لـه الإحكام شرح درر الحكام لمنلاخسرو، في اثني عشر مجلداً، ت ١٠٦٢هـ، وهو والد الشيخ عبد الغني النابلسي صاحب المؤلفات الكثيرة المشهورة، ت١١٤٣هـ . هدية العارفين ٢١٨/١.
٣١- الأوزجندي، لعله غالباً أراد قاضي خان حسن بن منصور الأوزجندي، صاحب الفتاوى، وشرح الجامع الصغير، والجامع الكبير، لمحمد بن الحسن، ت٥٩٢هـ. هدية العارفين ٢٨٠/١، تاج التراجم ص ١٥١.
۳۲- الباقاني، محمود بن بركات بن محمد نور الدين، نسبته إلى: (باقا)، من قرى نابلس وأصله منها فقيه حنفي دمشقي، لـه

Commentary
This passage is a biographical chapter that lists Hanafi scholars referenced in the commentary al-Lubab. It provides each scholar's full name, death date (Hijri), and often the source where more information can be found, such as 'al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah' or 'Hadiyyat al-‘Arifin'. The chapter serves as a quick reference for students to identify the authorities behind the rulings discussed. Notable figures include Abu Yusuf, the chief disciple of Abu Hanifah, and later commentators like Abu al-Fadl al-Mawsili and Akhi Zadeh. The author seems to compile these biographies to give context to the scholarly chain. The last entry (32) is incomplete, likely continuing on the next page.

Key Terms
الفوائد البهية (al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah): A biographical work on Hanafi scholars by Muhammad ‘Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi.
تاج التراجم (Taj al-Tarajim): A biographical dictionary of Hanafi scholars by Shams al-Din al-Sakhawi.
الجواهر المضية (al-Jawahir al-Mudiyyah): A biographical work on Hanafi scholars by Abu Bakr al-Mardini.
هدية العارفين (Hadiyyat al-‘Arifin): A biographical dictionary of authors by Isma‘il Basha al-Baghdadi.

Biography of Akhi Zadah 'Abd al-Halim al-Rumi
Listing biographical details of a Hanafi scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key works of Akhi Zadah and explain his role in the Hanafi scholarly tradition.

Core Idea
Akhi Zadah's glosses on Ibn Nujaym and al-Hidayah are vital links in the Hanafi chain of transmission.

This lesson introduces Akhi Zadah 'Abd al-Halim al-Rumi, a prominent Hanafi judge and commentator from the Ottoman period. His works, including glosses on al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair and al-Hidayah, exemplify the tradition of scholarly commentary in the Hanafi school. Understanding the lives and contributions of such scholars helps us appreciate the development of Hanafi fiqh and the authority of its texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and title
Read the Arabic entry and note the full name: Akhi Zadah 'Abd al-Halim ibn Muhammad al-Rumi. The title 'al-Rumi' indicates his Ottoman Turkish origin, and 'Akhi Zadah' suggests a lineage of scholars.
The term 'al-Rumi' often refers to the Anatolian region.
2
Note his position and death year
He served as a judge (qadi) in the military of Rum Ili. His death year is 1013 AH (1604 CE), placing him in the late 10th/early 11th century AH.
Death dates help establish scholarly chronology and teacher-student chains.
3
List his major works
He authored: (1) a gloss (ta'liqah) on al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair by Ibn Nujaym, (2) a marginal commentary (hashiyah) on al-Durar wa al-Ghurur, (3) a marginal commentary on Sadr al-Shari'ah, and (4) a commentary (sharh) on al-Hidayah.
All four works are advanced commentaries on core Hanafi texts.
4
Understand the significance of each work
Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair is a work on Hanafi legal maxims (qawa'id); al-Durar wa al-Ghurur is a compendium of fatwas; Sadr al-Shari'ah's work is a usul al-fiqh text; and al-Hidayah is the seminal Hanafi fiqh manual. His glosses represent the 'mutakhkhirin' (later scholars) layer of the school.
These glosses often resolve ambiguities and harmonize differences in the early texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخي زاده عبد الحليم بن محمد الرومي، القاضي بعسكر روم إيلي، ت۱۰١٣هـ ، له تعليقة على الأشباه والنظائر، لابن نجيم، وحاشية على الدرر والغرر، وحاشية على صدر الشريعة، ولـه شـرح على الهداية هدية العارفين ٥٠٤/١.
Akhi Zadah 'Abd al-Halim ibn Muhammad al-Rumi, judge in the military of Rum Ili, died 1013 AH. He has a gloss on al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair by Ibn Nujaym, a marginal commentary on al-Durar wa al-Ghurur, a marginal commentary on Sadr al-Shari'ah, and a commentary on al-Hidayah. Hadiyat al-'Arifin 1/504.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This is a biographical entry from the third chapter of al-Lubab, which provides brief biographies of scholars mentioned in the work. Here we have information about Akhi Zadah 'Abd al-Halim al-Rumi, a Hanafi judge and scholar from the Ottoman era. He wrote important glosses and commentaries on key Hanafi texts, including a gloss on Ibn Nujaym's al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair, and marginal notes on al-Durar wa al-Ghurur and Sadr al-Shari'ah's commentary. His death year is 1013 AH (1604 CE).

Key Terms
أخي زاده (Akhi Zadah): Surname of 'Abd al-Halim al-Rumi, indicating a lineage of scholars.
الأشباه والنظائر (al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair): A work on Hanafi legal maxims by Ibn Nujaym.
الدرر والغرر (al-Durar wa al-Ghurur): A compendium of Hanafi fatwas by al-Haskafi.
الهداية (al-Hidayah): The seminal Hanafi fiqh manual by al-Marghinani.
صدر الشريعة (Sadr al-Shari'ah): A Hanafi scholar known for his work in usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What year did Akhi Zadah 'Abd al-Halim al-Rumi die?
A) 1013 AH
B) 1062 AH
C) 592 AH
D) 930 AH

Key Takeaway
Akhi Zadah 'Abd al-Halim al-Rumi (d. 1013 AH) was a Hanafi judge whose glosses on key texts form an essential part of the school's later literature.

Al-Isbijabi: A Hanafi Commentator of the 6th Century
Listing biographical details of a Hanafi scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the full name of al-Isbijabi, identify his two major commentaries, and recall his death period.

Core Idea
Al-Isbijabi authored two key Hanafi commentaries: Zad al-Fuqaha' and al-Hawi.

This passage introduces a notable Hanafi scholar from the late 6th century AH. Knowing the scholars and their works helps situate fiqh texts within their historical context. Al-Isbijabi's commentaries on Quduri and Tahawi are important references in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar
Locate the full name in the passage: al-Isbijabi Abu al-Ma'ali Baha al-Din Muhammad ibn Ahmad. Note his title and lineage.
2
Recognize his works
The passage mentions two commentaries: 'Zad al-Fuqaha'' on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and 'al-Hawi' on Mukhtasar al-Tahawi.
These are primary works for Hanafi fiqh study.
3
Note his death period
He died in the late 6th century AH (approximately 12th century CE). This places him in the era of later Hanafi scholarship.
Approximate dates help connect scholars to developments in the madhhab.
4
Contextualize his importance
His commentaries are part of the sharh (commentary) tradition, expanding on foundational texts like al-Quduri's Mukhtasar.
Understanding the purpose of commentaries aids in using them effectively.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإسبيجابي أبو المعالي بهاء الدين محمـد بـن أحمد، له شرح على مختصر القدوري، سماه زاد الفقهاء، والحاوي شـرح مختصر الطحاوي، ت في أواخر القرن السادس. تاج التراجم ص ٢٥٦، هدية العارفين ١٠٥/٢.
Al-Isbijabi Abu al-Ma'ali Baha al-Din Muhammad ibn Ahmad. He has a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, which he named Zad al-Fuqaha', and al-Hawi, a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Tahawi. He died in the late sixth century. Taj al-Tarajim p. 256, Hadiyat al-'Arifin 2/105.

Commentary
This entry introduces al-Isbijabi, a Hanafi scholar from the late 6th century AH (12th century CE). He authored two important commentaries: 'Zad al-Fuqaha'' on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, and 'al-Hawi' on al-Tahawi's Mukhtasar. His works are referenced in biographical dictionaries like Taj al-Tarajim and Hadiyat al-'Arifin.

Key Terms
الإسبيجابي (al-Isbijabi): Scholarly surname (nisba) referring to a place in Central Asia.
زاد الفقهاء (Zad al-Fuqaha'): Title of his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, meaning 'Provisions of the Jurists'.
الحاوي (al-Hawi): Title of his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, meaning 'The Comprehensive'.

Isma'il al-Ha'ik – A Hanafi Fatwa Compiler
Biographical entry for a Hanafi scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Isma'il al-Ha'ik and state his most famous work.

Core Idea
Isma'il al-Ha'ik compiled a key collection of Hanafi fatwas still referenced today.

This brief biographical note introduces Isma'il al-Ha'ik, a late Hanafi jurist from Damascus. His collection of fatwas (al-Fatawa) is an important resource for later Hanafi rulings. Knowing his biography helps you appreciate the continuity of the fatwa tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the full name and nisba
Read the Arabic name: Isma'il ibn 'Ali ibn Rajab al-Dimashqi. Note the laqab (nickname) 'Ibn al-Ha'ik'.
The name shows his lineage and origin: Damascus.
2
Recognize his scholarly contribution
The text says 'lahu al-Fatawa' meaning he authored/complied a work of fatwas. Remember that al-Fatawa refers to a book, not just the genre.
Later Hanafi fatwa collections like al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya are famous; this is an earlier compilation.
3
Memorize his death year
He died in 1113 AH (1701 CE). This places him in the later classical period, after the time of the mujtahids.
Knowing death dates helps contextualize a scholar's work in the chain of transmission.

Isma'il al-Ha'ik, Isma'il ibn 'Ali ibn Rajab al-Dimashqi, known as Ibn al-Ha'ik. He has al-Fatawa. Died 1113 AH. Hadiyat al-'Arifin 1/219.

Who Was Isma'il al-Nabulsi?
Biographical entry on a Hanafi scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Isma'il al-Nabulsi and state his key scholarly contribution and familial relation.

Core Idea
Isma'il al-Nabulsi authored a massive commentary on Mulla Khusraw's Durar al-Hukkam and was the father of the renowned 'Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulsi.

This lesson introduces a Hanafi scholar whose work remains a reference for the Durar al-Hukkam. Understanding his lineage and his commentary helps situate his contribution within the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scholar
Read the full name and note the key identifier: 'Isma'il, author of Sharh al-Durar'.
Sharh al-Durar refers to his commentary on Mulla Khusraw's Durar al-Hukkam.
2
Note His Major Work
His work 'al-Ihkam Sharh Durar al-Hukkam' is a commentary in twelve volumes, indicating its comprehensiveness.
The title translates to 'The Perfect Comment on the Pearls of Rulings'.
3
Establish Temporal Context
He died in 1062 AH (1652 CE), placing him in the 11th century AH, a period of mature Hanafi scholarship.
Knowing the century aids in situating his thought.
4
Recognize His Son
His son 'Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulsi is a famous Sufi and scholar of many works, died 1143 AH.
The son's fame sometimes overshadows the father's contribution.

Biography of al-Baqqani: A Hanafi Jurist and Commentator
Biographical details of al-Baqqani

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify al-Baqqani's full name, origin, madhhab, and list his major Hanafi legal works.

Core Idea
Al-Baqqani wrote essential Hanafi commentaries and completions, bridging early and later scholarship.

This biography introduces al-Baqqani, a Hanafi jurist originally from a village near Nablus who later settled in Damascus. His works, particularly 'Majra al-Anhar' and completions of 'al-Bahr al-Ra'iq' and 'Lisan al-Hukkam', are important tools for studying Hanafi fiqh. Knowing his biographical background helps you trace the chain of Hanafi authority and identify key sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's identity
State al-Baqqani's full name: Mahmud ibn Barakat ibn Muhammad Nur al-Din. Note his nisbah 'al-Baqqani' from the village 'Baqa' near Nablus.
The nisbah indicates geographical origin.
2
Note his madhhab and location
He is described as a Hanafi jurist (faqih hanafi) from Damascus. This places him within the Hanafi scholarly tradition and the Syrian school.
Damascus was a major center of Hanafi scholarship.
3
List his major works
Identify the four works mentioned: Majra al-Anhar (commentary on Multaqa al-Abhar), Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (completion), Takmilat Lisan al-Hukkam (completion), and Sharh al-Nuqayah (commentary).
These works are later Hanafi references, often cited in fatwa.
4
Record his death date and sources
He died in 1003 AH (1595 CE). The sources for his biography are given: Khulasat al-Athar, Hadiyat al-'Arifin, Kashf al-Zunun.
These are standard biographical dictionaries for Islamic scholars.

The Four Kings Who Ruled the World: Bukhtanassar
Historical list of four world rulers with faith classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four kings who ruled the entire world and distinguish between the believers and disbelievers among them.

Core Idea
Only two believers and two disbelievers ever ruled the whole world.

This short passage from al-Lubab provides a fascinating historical note about the four kings who ruled the entire world. Among them is Bukhtanassar (Nebuchadnezzar), the Babylonian king who destroyed Jerusalem. Understanding this classification helps us appreciate how our classical scholars viewed world history from an Islamic perspective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four kings
Read the passage and list the four kings mentioned: Sulayman, Alexander (Dhul Qarnayn), Nimrod, and Bukhtanassar.
Sulayman is a prophet, Alexander is believed to be Dhul Qarnayn from the Quran.
2
Classify by faith
Divide the four into two believers (Sulayman, Alexander) and two disbelievers (Nimrod, Bukhtanassar).
The classification is based on the tafsir tradition cited.
3
Note the timeframe
Bukhtanassar lived 500 years before Jesus. This helps contextualize his actions in biblical history.
The passage references Tafsir al-Qurtubi and Ibn Kathir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بختنصر، هو أحد الملوك الأربعة الذين ملكوا الدنيا، وهم مؤمنان: نبي الله سليمان عليه السلام والإسكندر المقدوني (ذو القرنين) وكافران: النمروذ، وبختنصر. وبختنصر كان ملك بابل، وهو الذي سلطه الله على اليهود، فقتلهم واستباحهم، وخرَّب عليهم بيت المقدس، وكان زمنه قبل المسيح عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام بخمسمائة عام. تفسير القرطبي 10/ ٢١٥ ، تفسير ابن كثير، أول سورة الإسراء.
Bukhtanassar (Nebuchadnezzar): He is one of the four kings who ruled the world. They are: two believers: the Prophet of Allah Sulayman (peace be upon him) and Alexander the Macedonian (Dhul Qarnayn); and two disbelievers: Nimrod and Bukhtanassar. Bukhtanassar was the king of Babylon, and he was the one whom Allah gave power over the Jews, so he killed them, took them as spoils, and destroyed the Bayt al-Maqdis (Jerusalem). His time was five hundred years before the Messiah Jesus (peace and blessings be upon him). Tafsir al-Qurtubi 10/215, Tafsir Ibn Kathir, beginning of Surah al-Isra.

Commentary
This entry is not about a Hanafi scholar but about the historical figure Nebuchadnezzar (Bukhtanassar). It lists him as one of four kings who ruled the entire world, distinguishing between believers and disbelievers. The information is sourced from Qur'anic commentaries: al-Qurtubi and Ibn Kathir, particularly regarding the destruction of Jerusalem.

Key Terms

ذو القرنين (Dhul Qarnayn): Alexander the Macedonian, considered a believer and one of the four world rulers.
النمروذ (Nimrod): The disbelieving king who opposed Prophet Ibrahim.

Core Idea
Al-Birjandi's commentaries connect key Hanafi texts across usul and furu'.

Biographical entries in the margins of our texts are not footnotes to skip—they are chains of transmission and authority. This lesson spotlights a scholar whose commentaries bridge foundational works in usul al-fiqh and furu'. Knowing who he is and what he wrote helps you navigate the Hanafi tradition's textual lineage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and epithet

This nisba indicates his origin, not necessarily his teaching location.
2
List his known works from the passage
The passage mentions two commentaries: one on al-Manar by al-Nasafi, and one on al-Nuqayah (an abridgment of al-Wiqayah). Understand what each base text covers.
Al-Manar is a classic in usul al-fiqh; al-Wiqayah is a standard Hanafi fiqh text.
3
Note his death date and its significance
He died in 932 AH (1526 CE). This places him in the late classical/early post-classical Hanafi tradition, after the major consolidators.
Compare with scholars like Ibn Nujaym (d. 970 AH) or al-Haskafi (d. 1088 AH).
4
Trace the source of this information
The entry cites 'Hadiyat al-'Arifin' (by Isma‘il Pasha al-Baghdadi), a biographical dictionary. Recognize that such sources authenticate the scholarly lineage.
This is part of the 'rijal al-madhhab' tradition, critical for evaluating fatwa authorities.

Al-Birjandi 'Abd al-'Ali ibn Muhammad. He has a commentary on al-Manar by al-Nasafi, and a commentary on al-Nuqayah, which is an abridgment of al-Wiqayah. Died 932 AH. Hadiyat al-'Arifin 1/586.

This lesson introduces you to Muhammad al-Birkawi, a prominent Ottoman Hanafi jurist and moralist. Though his biographical entry is short, his works have had a lasting impact on Hanafi fiqh and Islamic spirituality. We will explore his most famous writings and their place in the tradition.

Identifying Burhan al-A'imma: Two Hanafi Scholars
Biographical note identifying two scholars with the same laqab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two Hanafi scholars known as 'Burhan al-A'imma' and state each one's key work and death date.

Core Idea
Two Hanafi scholars share the title 'Burhan al-A'imma' — learn to distinguish them.

This lesson addresses a biographical ambiguity that appears in classical Hanafi sources. The title 'Burhan al-A'imma' ('Proof of the Imams') was given to at least two different scholars. Understanding who they are helps you avoid confusion when referencing their works and contributions. We will learn their names, death dates, and key writings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two possible identities
The text mentions two candidates: al-Mahbubi and al-Sadr al-Shahid. Write down their full names.
2
Note their key works
Al-Mahbubi wrote a commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir; al-Sadr al-Shahid is known as a Hanafi jurist. Identify which scholar is associated with which work.
3
Memorize death dates
Al-Mahbubi died 630 AH; al-Sadr al-Shahid died 536 AH. Use these dates to anchor them historically.
4
Understand the ambiguity
The text leaves the identity uncertain. Recognize that in later references, you may need to check the context to determine which scholar is meant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
برهان الأئمة المحبوبي عبيد الله بن إبراهيم جمال الدين البخاري، له شرح الجامع الصغير لمحمد بن الحسن، ت٦٣٠هـ. الفوائد البهية ص ۱۰۸ ، هدية العارفين ٦٤٩/١. أو المراد برهان الأئمة الحسام الشهيد وهو الصدر الشهيد عمـر ابن عبد العزيز بن مازه ت ٥٣٦هـ. تاج التراجم ص ٢١٧ .
Burhan al-A'imma al-Mahbubi 'Ubayd Allah ibn Ibrahim Jamal al-Din al-Bukhari. He has a commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan. Died 630 AH. Al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah p. 108, Hadiyat al-'Arifin 1/649. Or what is meant is Burhan al-A'imma al-Husam al-Shahid, who is al-Sadr al-Shahid 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Mazah, died 536 AH. Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This entry provides two possible identifications for 'Burhan al-A'imma'. The first is al-Mahbubi, 'Ubayd Allah al-Bukhari, a Hanafi scholar who wrote a commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir, dying in 630 AH (1233 CE). The second possibility is al-Husam al-Shahid, 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Mazah (al-Sadr al-Shahid), who died in 536 AH (1142 CE). The text leaves the identity uncertain.

Key Terms
برهان الأئمة المحبوبي (Burhan al-A'imma al-Mahbubi): The title given to 'Ubayd Allah ibn Ibrahim al-Bukhari, a Hanafi scholar who wrote a commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir and died 630 AH.

Why Biographies Matter in Hanafi Fiqh
Biographical appendix listing Hanafi scholars with dates and works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the purpose of biographical entries in a Hanafi fiqh text and identify the authority weight of a scholar based on the information provided.

Core Idea
Knowing a scholar's era and works determines the authority of their legal opinion in the Hanafi school.

This passage from Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri is a biographical appendix listing many Hanafi jurists mentioned throughout the text. While it may seem like mere historical data, these biographies serve a critical function: they allow the reader to gauge the authority (tabaqah) of each scholar. In Hanafi fiqh, later scholars may weigh the opinions of earlier authorities differently, and knowing who wrote which commentary helps the mufti determine the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and death date
Scan the entry for the name and year (e.g., ت٩٣٢ هـ). This places the scholar in history and helps determine their generation.
Death dates are often given in the Hijri calendar; note the century.
2
Note any titles or honorifics
Titles like 'برهان الأئمة' or 'صاحب المحيط' indicate the scholar's renown and specialization.
Titles can reveal a scholar's role, e.g., 'al-mufti' or 'al-faqih'.
3
List the main works mentioned
Works like 'الطريقة المحمدية' or 'شرح الوقاية' tell us their contributions to Hanafi literature.
Knowing the type of work (e.g., commentary, fatwa collection) helps assess its authority.
4
Check the cross-reference to other sources
The text cites sources like 'هدية العارفين' and 'كشف الظنون', which are standard biographical dictionaries.
These cross-references allow you to verify and deepen your knowledge of the scholar.
5
Assess the authority level
Based on the period and works, determine if the scholar is from the mutaqaddimin (early) or muta'akhkhirin (later) layer, which affects the weight of their opinions.
Earlier scholars generally have higher authority unless later scholars explicitly adopt their view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث: ترجمة موجزة للأعلام المذكورين في اللباب
عدة مصنفات منها : مجرى الأنهر شرح ملتقى الأبحر، وتكملة البحر الرائق، وتكملة لسان الحكام وشرح النقاية، ت١٠٠٣هـ. خلاصة الأثر ٣١٧/٤ ، هدية العارفين ٤١٤/٢ ، كشف الظنون ١٨١٤/٢. ٣٣ بختنصر، هو أحد الملوك الأربعة الذين ملكوا الدنيا، وهم
-90.
مؤمنان: نبي الله سليمان عليه السلام والإسكندر المقدوني (ذو القرنين وكافران: النمروذ، وبختنصر.
وبختنصر كان ملك بابل، وهو الذي سلطه الله على اليهود، فقتلهم واستباحهم، وخرَّب عليهم بيت المقدس، وكان زمنه قبل المسيح عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام بخمسمائة عام. تفسير القرطبي

Commentary
This passage is the third chapter of Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, providing brief biographical notes on notable figures mentioned in the text. These include later Hanafi jurists, commentators, and even historical figures like Bukhtanassar. The biographies help readers understand the authority and period of each scholar, which is essential for evaluating the weight of their opinions within the Hanafi school. The author compiles information from standard biographical sources such as Hadiyat al-'Arifin and Kashf al-Zunun.

Key Terms
الفقيه الحنفي (al-faqih al-hanafi): A jurist who follows the Hanafi school of Islamic law.
صاحب المحيط (sahib al-muhit): Author of the work 'Al-Muhit', a comprehensive Hanafi fiqh text.
شرح الوقاية (sharh al-wiqayah): A commentary on the Hanafi legal text 'Al-Wiqayah'.

Life of the Author

Key Hanafi Authorities in Al-Lubab
Biographical dictionary of Hanafi scholars referenced in Al-Lubab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major Hanafi scholars cited in Al-Lubab and state their key fiqh works, establishing their authority in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Knowing the scholars behind the rulings strengthens your understanding of the Hanafi proof structure and textual hierarchy.

This lesson introduces the biographical appendix of Al-Lubab, which lists the Hanafi masters whose works are cited throughout the commentary. Understanding who these scholars are — their time, their teachers, and their major texts — allows you to weigh the authority of different opinions and trace the chain of transmission. The appendix serves as a 'who's who' for students of the Hanafi school, explaining the authority behind the rulings in Al-Lubab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and any honorifics
Scan the entry for the scholar's full name (including kunya, laqab, nisba) and any honorifics like 'Shams al-A'imma' or 'Hafiz al-Din'. This helps place them in the Hanafi scholarly lineage.
Honorifics often indicate the scholar's prominence; e.g., 'Shams al-A'imma' means 'Sun of the Imams'.
2
Note the scholar's key fiqh work(s)
Each scholar is associated with one or more major works. Record these, as they are frequently cited in Al-Lubab and later Hanafi texts.
Examples: al-Muhit (Radi al-Din), al-Kafi (al-Hakim al-Shahid), al-Kanz (al-Nasafi).
3
Record the death date (or century)
The death date (e.g., 576 AH) places the scholar in the historical chain of transmission. This helps assess which works are earlier or later, affecting their authority.
Earlier scholars like al-Hasan ibn Ziyad (d. 204 AH) are closer to Abu Hanifa; later ones like Hamid Afandi (d. 1171 AH) represent the later tradition.
4
Cross-reference other biographical sources
The appendix cites sources like Taj al-Tarajim and Hadiyat al-Arifin. Use these to verify details and understand the broader scholarly consensus on the scholar's status.
This step trains you to approach biographical notes critically, recognizing that later sources may refine earlier accounts.
5
Understand the role of each work in the Hanafi madhhab hierarchy
Determine whether the work is part of Zahir al-Riwayah, Nawadir, or later fatwa collections. This classification affects the epistemological weight of the rulings derived from that work.
For example, al-Muhit and al-Kafi are from the Zahir al-Riwayah corpus, giving them high authority; al-Fatawa al-Hamidiyya is a later fatwa collection.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical list from Al-Lubab, providing short biographies of Hanafi scholars cited in the main text. The author lists them numerically, giving each scholar's full name, key works, death date, and biographical sources like Taj al-Tarajim and Hadiyat al-Arifin. These scholars are foundational figures in the Hanafi school. For example, Radi al-Din (d. 576 AH) wrote al-Muhit, a major reference; al-Hakim al-Shahid (d. 334 AH) authored al-Kafi, an early mukhtasar; Hamid Afandi al-'Imadi (d. 1171 AH) produced the Hamidiyya Fatawa later annotated by Ibn 'Abidin. The list also includes teachers of major Hanafi imams like al-Hasan ibn Ziyad (d. 204 AH), a direct student of Abu Hanifa. The entry on Jamal al-Islam (= Baha al-Din al-Isbijabi) clarifies a cross-reference in manuscripts. This section serves as a who's-who for students of the Hanafi tradition, explaining the authority behind the rulings in Al-Lubab.

Key Terms
المحيط (al-Muhit): A comprehensive Hanafi fiqh work by Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi, referenced in the index of sources of Al-Lubab.
زاد الفقهاء (Zad al-Fuqaha'): A Hanafi fiqh text by Baha al-Din al-Isbijabi (Jamal al-Islam), used as a source for citations in Al-Lubab.
الكنز (al-Kanz): Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi's well-known Hanafi fiqh manual, referred to as 'Hafiz al-Din' in the text.
