Reading Hanafi Biographical Entries: Scholars of al-Lubab
Biographical list of Hanafi scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract key biographical data (full name, death date, major works) from a classical Hanafi biographical entry and explain its relevance to the legal text.

Core Idea
Biographical entries reveal the chain of transmission and authority behind Hanafi rulings.

This chapter from al-Lubab presents brief biographies of the jurists mentioned in the commentary. These entries are not part of the legal text itself but serve as a reference for understanding the scholarly pedigree of each authority cited. Learning to read these entries helps you appreciate the depth and continuity of the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and key title
Read the entry carefully. Note any honorific titles like 'Rukn al-A'imma' (Pillar of the Imams) or 'al-Sadidi' which indicate the scholar's rank. Also note nisbas that show geographic origin, e.g., al-Khujandi (from Khujand).
Some names have multiple parts; look for the death date to confirm identity.
2
Note the death date (tarih al-wafat)
The death date places the scholar in a specific century and can link him to teachers and students. For example, Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl died in 158 AH, making him a contemporary of Abu Hanifah.
Beware of variant dates noted by 'قيل' (it is said).
3
List the scholar's major works
Works like al-Mabsut, al-Hiyal, or Sharh Kanz al-Daqa'iq indicate the scholar's area of specialization. This helps you know which texts he contributed to the madhhab.
Some works are glosses (hashiyah) on earlier texts.
4
Identify teacher-student relationships
Look for phrases like 'صاحب الإمام أبي حنيفة' (companion of Imam Abu Hanifah) or 'تفقه على فلان' (studied under so-and-so). These chains (silsila) are crucial for isnad in fiqh.
The entry for Rukn al-A'imma al-Sabbighi mentions he studied under Abu al-Yusr al-Bazdawi.
5
Relate the scholar to the text of al-Lubab
Ask: Why is this scholar mentioned in the commentary? Is he cited as an authority? Does his work comment on al-Quduri? This connects the biography to the main text being studied.
For example, al-Sabbighi wrote a commentary on al-Quduri itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث: ترجمة موجزة للأعلام المذكورين في اللباب
49 - الخجندي، لعله جلال الدين الخجندي عمر بن محمد بن عمر الخبازي، له حاشية على الهداية والفتاوى، والمغني في أصول الفقه، ت 691هـ. هدية العارفين 787/1، تاج التراجم ص 220.
50 - الخصاف أبو بكر أحمد بن عمرو (عمر)، له الحيل، والخراج، والمناسك، ت 261هـ. تاج التراجم ص 97.
51 - خليل الكاملي صاحب الحاشية على رسالة الإسطرلاب خليل بن عبد السلام الدمشقي، ت 1207هـ. حلية البشر 591/1.
52 - خواهر زاده محمد بن الحسين المعروف ببكر خواهر زاده البخاري له المختصر، والتجنيس، والمبسوط ت 483هـ. الفوائد البهية ص 163. ومعنى: خُواهَر زاده أي ابن أخت عالم، والمترجم هو ابن أخت القاضي أبي ثابت محمد بن أحمد البخاري.
53 - الخير الرملي، خير الدين بن أحمد بن نور الدين علي الأيوبي العليمي الفاروقي، له حاشية على الأشباه والنظائر، وحاشية على كنز الدقائق والفتاوى، ت 1081هـ. هدية العارفين 358/1.
54 - الرستُغْفَني علي بن سعيد من كبار مشايخ سمرقند، من أجل أصحاب أبي منصور الماتريدي له إرشاد المهتدي، ت نحو 345هـ، الأعلام 4/291، الفوائد البهية ص 65، تاج التراجم ص 205.
55 - ركن الأئمة الصبّاغي عبد الكريم بن محمد أبو المكارم، له شرح على القدوري، وقد تفقه على أبي اليسر البزدوي المديني، المتوفى سنة 493هـ، وعليه فهو من علماء القرن الخامس، وبداية السادس، الجواهر المضية 456/2، هدية العارفين 608/1.
56 - ركن الأئمة الوالجاني، لعله هو ركن الدين الوالجاني الخوارزمي، كان إماماً جليلاً كثير العلم، مجتهد زمانه في المذهب والخلاف، تفقه عليه صاحب القنية الزاهدي، المتوفى سنة 658هـ، الفوائد البهية ص 74، الجواهر المضية 338/4، 388.
57 - زفر بن الهذيل البصري، صاحب الإمام أبي حنيفة، إمام أئمة المسلمين، فقيه من فقهاء المحدثين، ت 158هـ. تاج التراجم ص 169.
58 - الزوزني السديدي محمد بن محمود بن محمد تاج الدين أبو المفاخر، شرح منظومة النسفي، ت 699هـ، وقيل 665هـ، وقيل 575هـ. تاج التراجم، مع تعليقات محققه ص 279، هدية العارفين 140/2.
59 - الزيلعي، هو فخر الدين عثمان بن علي بن محمد الزيلعي، صاحب تبيين الحقائق شرح كنز الدقائق وشرح الجامع الكبير، لمحمد بن الحسن، وشرح المختار للموصلي، ت 743هـ. تاج التراجم ص 204، هدية العارفين 655/1. وهناك جمال الدين الزيلعي يوسف بن عبد الله (وسماه جماعة: عبد الله بن يوسف)، صاحب نصب الراية، وهو تلميذ فخر الدين، ت 762هـ. هدية العارفين 557/2.
60 - السديدي = الزوزني السديدي.
61 - سعد بن معاذ المروزي أبو عصمة، ذكره القرشي في
Chapter Three: Brief Biography of the Notable Figures Mentioned in al-Lubab
49 - al-Khujandi, perhaps Jalal al-Din al-Khujandi 'Umar ibn Muhammad ibn 'Umar al-Khabbazi, he has a gloss on al-Hidayah and al-Fatawa, and al-Mughni fi Usul al-Fiqh, d. 691 AH. Hadiyyat al-'Arifin 1/787, Taj al-Tarajim p. 220.
50 - al-Khassaf Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn 'Amr ('Umar), he has al-Hiyal, al-Kharaj, and al-Manasik, d. 261 AH. Taj al-Tarajim p. 97.
51 - Khalil al-Kamili, author of the gloss on Risalah al-Isturlab, Khalil ibn 'Abd al-Salam al-Dimashqi, d. 1207 AH. Hilyat al-Bashar 1/591.
52 - Khwaharzadah Muhammad ibn al-Husayn known as Bakr Khwaharzadah al-Bukhari, he has al-Mukhtasar, al-Tajnis, and al-Mabsut, d. 483 AH. al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah p. 163. And meaning: Khwaharzadah is 'son of a scholar's sister', and the translated one is the nephew of the judge Abu Thabit Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Bukhari.
53 - al-Khayr al-Ramli, Khayr al-Din ibn Ahmad ibn Nur al-Din 'Ali al-Ayyubi al-'Ulaymi al-Faruqi, he has a gloss on al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir and a gloss on Kanz al-Daqa'iq and al-Fatawa, d. 1081 AH. Hadiyyat al-'Arifin 1/358.
54 - al-Rustughfani 'Ali ibn Sa'id, from the senior shaykhs of Samarqand, from the greatest companions of Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, he has Irshad al-Muhtadi, d. around 345 AH. al-A'lam 4/291, al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah p. 65, Taj al-Tarajim p. 205.
55 - Rukn al-A'imma al-Sabbighi 'Abd al-Karim ibn Muhammad Abu al-Makarim, he has a commentary on al-Quduri, and he studied under Abu al-Yusr al-Bazdawi al-Madini, died 493 AH, thus he is from scholars of the 5th century and beginning of the 6th, al-Jawahir al-Mudiyyah 2/456, Hadiyyat al-'Arifin 1/608.
56 - Rukn al-A'imma al-Waljani, perhaps Rukn al-Din al-Waljani al-Khwarizmi, he was a great imam with much knowledge, a mujtahid of his time in madhhab and polemics, the author of al-Qunyah al-Zahidi studied under him, died 658 AH. al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah p. 74, al-Jawahir al-Mudiyyah 4/338, 388.
57 - Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl al-Basri, companion of Imam Abu Hanifah, imam of the imams of the Muslims, a jurist from the jurists of the hadith scholars, d. 158 AH. Taj al-Tarajim p. 169.
58 - al-Zawzani al-Sadidi Muhammad ibn Mahmud ibn Muhammad Taj al-Din Abu al-Mafakhir, commentator on Manzumah al-Nasafi, d. 699 AH, and it is said 665 AH, and it is said 575 AH. Taj al-Tarajim with comments of its editor p. 279, Hadiyyat al-'Arifin 2/140.
59 - al-Zayla'i, he is Fakhr al-Din 'Uthman ibn 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Zayla'i, author of Tabyin al-Haqa'iq Sharh Kanz al-Daqa'iq and Sharh al-Jami' al-Kabir by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, and Sharh al-Mukhtar by al-Mawsili, d. 743 AH. Taj al-Tarajim p. 204, Hadiyyat al-'Arifin 1/655. And there is Jamal al-Din al-Zayla'i Yusuf ibn 'Abd Allah (and some named him 'Abd Allah ibn Yusuf), author of Nasb al-Rayah, and he is a student of Fakhr al-Din, d. 762 AH. Hadiyyat al-'Arifin 2/557.
60 - al-Sadidi = al-Zawzani al-Sadidi.
61 - Sa'd ibn Mu'adh al-Marwazi Abu 'Ismah, al-Qurashi mentioned him in
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is a biographical chapter from al-Lubab, which lists notable Hanafi scholars whose names appear in the text. It provides concise entries with their full names, key works, death dates, and references to standard biographical sources. Each entry serves as a quick reference for the reader to identify the scholar's stature and contributions to the Hanafi madhhab.

Entries include scholars from different periods, such as al-Khassaf (d. 261 AH), an early Hanafi jurist known for works on legal stratagems (al-Hiyal) and taxation (al-Kharaj); Khwaharzadah (d. 483 AH), who wrote al-Mabsut, a foundational Hanafi work; Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl (d. 158 AH), a direct student of Abu Hanifah; and later commentators like al-Zayla'i (d. 743 AH), author of Tabyin al-Haqa'iq. The list also includes lesser-known figures like al-Rustughfani and al-Waljani, demonstrating the breadth of the Hanafi tradition.

The phrase "خواهر زاده" is explained as meaning 'sister's son,' indicating a scholarly lineage. This reflects the Hanafi tradition of transmitting knowledge through familial and teacher-student networks.

Key Terms
خواهر زاده (khwaharzadah): Literally 'sister's son,' i.e., nephew; used as a title for a scholar who is the nephew of a prominent scholar.
ركن الأئمة (Rukn al-A'imma): Title meaning 'Pillar of the Imams', indicating a highly respected scholar.
صاحب الإمام أبي حنيفة (sahib al-Imam Abi Hanifah): Companion of Imam Abu Hanifah, meaning a direct student or close associate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl
C) al-Zayla'i
D) al-Rustughfani

Key Takeaway
Biographical entries in Hanafi works are not mere decoration; they reveal the chain of transmission and authority behind the legal rulings.

Key Hanafi Scholars in al-Lubab (56–67)
Biographical list of Hanafi scholars 56–67

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major Hanafi scholars listed in al-Lubab's biographical chapter and state their key works and contributions to the madhhab.

Core Idea
Knowing the scholars behind the texts anchors the authority of rulings.

Al-Lubab, al-Maydani's commentary on al-Quduri, includes a biographical appendix of scholars cited. This lesson covers entries 56 to 67, highlighting figures like Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl, al-Zayla'i, and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi. Understanding who these scholars are and their place in the Hanafi tradition helps you assess the weight of their opinions in fiqh discussions.

Guided Path
1
Scan the Scholar List
Read through entries 56–67 to get a sense of the range of scholars—from early students of Abu Hanifa to later commentators.
2
Identify Generations
Group the scholars by century: Zufar (2nd century), Sa'd ibn Mu'adh (3rd century), al-Sarakhsi (5th-6th century), al-Zayla'i, al-Jurjani (8th century), etc.
This helps understand the chronological development of the Hanafi school.
3
Note Key Works
For each scholar, note the major work(s) mentioned. For example, al-Sarakhsi's al-Mabsut, al-Zayla'i's Tabyin al-Haqa'iq.
These are important sources for Hanafi fiqh.
4
Recognize Relationships
Pay attention to teacher-student links, e.g., al-Zahidi studied under al-Waljani; al-Zayla'i's student Jamal al-Din al-Zayla'i wrote Nasb al-Rayah.
These networks show transmission of knowledge.
5
Reflect on Significance
Consider why al-Maydani included each scholar. Most are authorities whose opinions are cited in the commentary.
This elevates the passage from mere biography to a key to understanding the text's intellectual heritage.

When he reached the chapter on conditions (shurut), he was released, and he also wrote Sharh Kitab al-Kasb by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, and Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, d. 490 AH. Taj al-Tarajim p.234.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage is from al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, a commentary on al-Quduri's matn. The author, al-Maydani, includes a chapter of brief biographies of scholars mentioned in the commentary. These entries serve to identify the authorities cited, their works, and their relationships within the Hanafi tradition. The list numbers scholars from 56 to 67, with some numbering irregularities. Notable entries include Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl, a direct student of Abu Hanifa; al-Zayla'i, author of Tabyin al-Haqa'iq; and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, the famous Hanafi jurist who dictated al-Mabsut while imprisoned. The compiler relies on sources like al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya, Taj al-Tarajim, and Hadiyyat al-Arifin. The biographical details help students contextualize the legal opinions in al-Lubab.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubab): Refers to the book 'al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab' by al-Maydani, a commentary on al-Quduri's mukhtasar.
المبسوط (al-Mabsut): A major Hanafi fiqh work by al-Sarakhsi, a commentary on al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid, dictated from memory while imprisoned.
تبيين الحقائق (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq): A commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq by Fakhr al-Din al-Zayla'i, widely used in Hanafi fiqh.
شافعي (al-Shafi'i): Imam Muhammad ibn Idris al-Shafi'i, founder of the Shafi'i school, mentioned only as a reference, not a Hanafi scholar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The biographical appendix in al-Lubab introduces the scholarly authorities behind the commentary, helping students understand the transmission and hierarchy of Hanafi knowledge.

Life of the Author

Biographical Sketches of Hanafi Scholars in al-Lubab
Biographical reference section with brief scholar notices.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major Hanafi scholars cited in al-Lubab, state their key works, and classify them by historical period.

Core Idea
Knowing the authors behind the fiqh texts is essential for assessing authority and reliability.

Al-Lubab frequently cites earlier Hanafi authorities. This biographical appendix provides brief notices on these scholars. Understanding their background and works helps readers evaluate the strength of the transmitted opinions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and death date
Each entry gives a name and often a death date. This anchors the figure in a specific century and helps establish their place in the chain of transmission.
Death dates are crucial for determining contemporaneity with other scholars.
2
Note the major works attributed to them
Especially those works cited in al-Lubab. For example, al-Sarakhsi's al-Mabsut and al-Tahawi's Mukhtasar are foundational Hanafi texts.
Works like al-Mabsut are from the Zahir al-Riwayah corpus.
3
Determine madhhab affiliation
Most are Hanafi, but some (like al-Shafi'i) are from other schools. Distinguishing is important for understanding the perspective of the cited opinion.
The commentator sometimes explicitly states the madhhab.
4
Observe notes of uncertainty
The commentator uses words like 'perhaps' or 'I could not determine' for some figures (e.g., al-Sayrafi). This signals weaker authority or disputed identity.
Such uncertainty affects how much weight to give a citation from that scholar.
5
Reflect on the chain of transmission
Consider how each scholar connects to earlier authorities. For instance, al-Sarakhsi comments on al-Hakim al-Shahid's al-Kafi, who in turn transmits from earlier Hanafi masters.
This chain establishes the reliability of the legal rulings transmitted.

٦٦ - شمس الأئمة، لعله الحلواني = الحلواني. أو شمس الأئمة السرخسي = شمس الأئمة السرخسي.
٦٧ - شمس الأئمة السرخسي محمد بن أحمد، صاحب المبسوط شرح الكافي للحاكم الشهيد الذي أملاه من خاطره وهو محبوس في الجب، كلمة نصح بها الحاكم، وأملى أصول بسبب الفقه، ثم أملى شرح السير الكبير لمحمد بن الحسن، ولما وصل فيه إلى باب الشروط حَصَلَ له الفَرَج، فأطلق، وله شرح كتاب الكسب لمحمد بن الحسن، وله شرح مختصر الطحاوي، ت ٤٩٠ هـ. تاج التراجم ص ٢٣٤.
٦٨ - الشمنِّي أحمد بن كمال الدين محمد بن محمد الحسن المصري تقي الدين الفقيه الحنفي له أوفق المسالك لتأدية المناسك، وعالي الرتبة في شرح نظم النخبة، لوالده، وكمال الدراية في شرح النقاية، وغيرها، ت ٨٧٢هـ . هدية العارفين ١٣٢/١. أما والده، فهو كمال الدين محمد بن محمد الفقيه المالكي، ت ٨٢١هـ ، له نظم نخبة الفكر في المصطلح للحافظ ابن حجر العسقلاني هدية العارفين ١٨٣/٢.
٦٩ - شيخ الإسلام الحارثي محمود بن عبيد الله الحارثي المروزي، من كبار أئمة المذهب والخلاف له العون في الفقه، ت ٦٠٦ هـ. الفوائد البهية ص ٢٠٩.
٧٠ - صاحب المجمع في شرحه، لعله غالباً مجمع البحرين، لمظفر الدين بن الساعاتي أحمد بن علي، وله البديع في أصول الفقه، ت ٧٩٤هـ. تاج التراجم ص ٩٥.
الصدر (الشهيد) = الحسام الشهيد.
صدر الشريعة : اشتهر به اثنان أكبر وأصغر. الفوائد ص ٢٤٥
٧١ - الصيرفي ؟ لم أستطع تحديد من أراد، لكنه قبل سنة ٨٠٠هـ، حيث نقل عنه الحدادي صاحب الجوهرة النيرة، المتوفى سنة ٨٠٠هـ.
٧٢ - الطحاوي أحمد بن محمد أبو جعفر، صاحب المختصر، وشرح معاني الآثار، ت ٣٢١هـ. تاج التراجم ص ١٠٠.
٧٣ - الطحطاوي (الطهطاوي) أحمد بن محمد بن إسماعيل، صاحب الحاشية على مراقي الفلاح شرح نور الإيضاح للشرنبلالي
Chapter Three: A brief biography of the notables mentioned in al-Lubab. [251] Al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya 4/66, and that Hafiz al-Din al-Nasafi mentioned him in his commentary on al-Hidayah, likewise al-Sighnaqi in his book al-Karahiyyah, and his death date is not mentioned, and he is from the scholars of the 3rd century AH. 62 - Sa'di Efendi, perhaps Sa'di Chalabi Sa'dullah ibn 'Isa (d. 945 AH), author of the gloss on al-'Inayah on al-Hidayah. 63 - al-Sayyid al-Jurjani al-Sharif 'Ali ibn Muhammad, among his most famous books is al-Ta'rifat, d. 792 AH. al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah p. 125. 64 - al-Shafi'i, the famous Imam, founder of the madhhab, Muhammad ibn Idris, d. 204 AH. 65 - al-Qadi Shurayh ibn al-Harith ibn Qays al-Kindi, among the most famous judges in early Islam, originally from Yemen, served as judge of Kufa during the time of our master 'Uthman, 'Ali, and Mu'awiyah (may Allah be pleased with them), he lived long, d. 78 AH. al-A'lam 3/161, Shadharat al-Dhahab 1/85. 66 - Shams al-A'imma, perhaps al-Halwani = al-Halwani, or Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi = Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi. 67 - Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi Muhammad ibn Ahmad, author of al-Mabsut, a commentary on al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid which he dictated from his mind while imprisoned in a pit, a word of advice to the judge, he dictated principles of fiqh, then dictated the commentary on al-Siyar al-Kabir by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, and when he reached the chapter on conditions, he was relieved, so he was released. He also authored a commentary on Kitab al-Kasb by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, and a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Tahawi. d. 490 AH. Taj al-Tarajim p. 234. 68 - al-Shimnni Ahmad ibn Kamal al-Din Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Hasan al-Misri Taqi al-Din, a Hanafi jurist, author of Awfaq al-Masalik li-Ta'diyat al-Manasik, and 'Ali al-Rutbah fi Sharh Nazm al-Nukhbah, by his father, and Kamal al-Dirayah fi Sharh al-Niqayah, and others, d. 872 AH. Hadiyyat al-'Arifin 1/132. As for his father, he is Kamal al-Din Muhammad ibn Muhammad, a Maliki jurist, d. 821 AH, author of Nazm Nukhbat al-Fikr in terminology of hadith by Ibn Hajar al-'Asqalani, Hadiyyat al-'Arifin 2/183. 69 - Shaykh al-Islam al-Harithi Mahmud ibn 'Ubayd Allah al-Harithi al-Marwazi, among the leading imams of the madhhab and debate, author of al-'Awn in fiqh, d. 606 AH. al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah p. 209. 70 - The author of al-Majma' in its commentary, perhaps mainly Majma' al-Bahrayn, by Muzaffar al-Din ibn al-Sa'ati Ahmad ibn 'Ali, also authored al-Badi' in usul al-fiqh, d. 794 AH. Taj al-Tarajim p. 95. al-Sadr (al-Shahid) = al-Husam al-Shahid. Sadr al-Shari'ah: two are known by this, the greater and the lesser. al-Fawa'id p. 245. 71 - al-Sayrafi? I could not determine who is intended, but he is before the year 800 AH, as al-Haddadi, author of al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, d. 800 AH, narrated from him. 72 - al-Tahawi Ahmad ibn Muhammad Abu Ja'far, author of al-Mukhtasar and Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar, d. 321 AH. Taj al-Tarajim p. 100. 73 - al-Tahtawi (al-Tahrawi) Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Isma'il, author of the gloss on Maraqi al-Falah Sharh Nur al-Idah by al-Shurunbulali.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a biographical reference section from al-Lubab, providing brief notices on scholars cited in the commentary. It serves as a quick guide for the reader to identify the authorities behind the legal discussions. The entries range from early figures like Shurayh (a companion-era judge) to later Hanafi authorities like Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi (d. 490 AH), whose magnum opus al-Mabsut is foundational in the Hanafi school. Al-Sarakhsi's dramatic dictation of al-Mabsut while imprisoned is noted, highlighting his scholarly dedication. Other notable Hanafis include al-Tahawi (d. 321 AH), whose Mukhtasar is a key text, and al-Tahtawi (d. after 800 AH), known for his glosses. Non-Hanafis like al-Shafi'i and al-Jurjani are included for reference. The passage also clarifies ambiguities: 'Shams al-A'imma' could refer to either al-Halwani or al-Sarakhsi, and 'al-Sayrafi' remains unidentified. The compiler occasionally notes his uncertainty, e.g., 'perhaps al-Halwani' and 'I could not determine who is intended'.

Key Terms
شمس الأئمة السرخسي (Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi): Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Sarakhsi (d. 490 AH), a leading Hanafi faqih and author of al-Mabsut, a comprehensive commentary on al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid. He dictated his works while imprisoned.
الطحاوي (al-Tahawi): Ahmad ibn Muhammad Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi (d. 321 AH), a Hanafi jurist famous for his Mukhtasar (a condensed fiqh text) and Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar (a hadith commentary).
المبسوط (al-Mabsut): The encyclopedic Hanafi fiqh work by al-Sarakhsi, commentary on al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid.
الحاكم الشهيد (al-Hakim al-Shahid): Abu al-Fadl Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Marwazi (d. 334 AH), author of al-Kafi, a foundational Hanafi text.
الهداية (al-Hidayah): A seminal Hanafi fiqh work by Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani (d. 593 AH), widely studied and commented upon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Hanafi Scholars in al-Lubab
Biographical appendix listing Hanafi scholars and their works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major Hanafi scholars listed in al-Lubab and state their most significant works.

Core Idea
Knowing the scholars behind the texts is essential for weighing authority in Hanafi fiqh.

This passage from al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri provides brief biographies of Hanafi scholars whose names appear in the commentary. Recognizing their eras and works helps you understand the chain of transmission and the weight of their opinions. In this lesson, we introduce the most frequently cited figures: al-Tahawi, al-Haskafi, and al-Bazdawi, as well as clarify the honorific 'Sadr al-Shari'ah'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's name and honorific
Carefully read each entry and note the full name, including any titles like 'Shaykh al-Islam' or 'Fakhr al-Islam'.
Titles indicate the scholar's reputation and authority within the madhhab.
2
Record the death date and era
Each entry includes a death date (e.g., 321 AH for al-Tahawi). This places the scholar in the historical development of the Hanafi school.
Earlier scholars (e.g., al-Tahawi) are foundational; later ones (e.g., al-Haskafi) are commentators and synthesizers.
3
List the major works
Each biography mentions key writings. For example, al-Tahawi wrote 'al-Mukhtasar', al-Haskafi wrote 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar'.
These works are frequently referenced in later fiqh texts and fatwas.
4
Understand their role in the madhhab
Determine whether the scholar is a primary authority, a commentator, or a later compiler. For instance, al-Bazdawi is a major usuli authority.
The role affects how their opinions are weighted in tarjih.
5
Cross-reference with biographical sources
The passage cites sources like 'Hadiyat al-'Arifin'. Note which external dictionary provides further details.
This trains you to use scholarly tools for verification.

الفصل الثالث: ترجمة موجزة للأعلام المذكورين في اللباب

الشمنِّي أحمد بن كمال الدين محمد بن محمد الحسن المصري تقي الدين الفقيه الحنفي له أوفق المسالك لتأدية المناسك، وعالي الرتبة في شرح نظم النخبة ، لوالده، وكمال الدراية في شرح النقاية، وغيرها، ت ٨٧٢هـ . هدية العارفين ١٣٢/١. أما والده، فهو كمال الدين محمد بن محمد الفقيه المالكي، ت ٨٢١هـ ، له نظم نخبة الفكر في المصطلح للحافظ ابن حجـ العسقلاني هدية العارفين .۱۸۳/۲

٦٩ - شيخ الإسلام الحارثي محمود بن عبيد الله الحارثي المروزي، من كبار أئمة المذهب والخلاف له العون في الفقه، ت ٦٠٦ هـ. الفوائد البهية ص ۲۰۹.

٧٠- صاحب المجمع في شرحه، لعلـه غالباً مجمع البحرين ، لمظفر الدين بن الساعاتي أحمد بن علي، وله البديع في أصول الفقه، ت ٧٩٤هـ. تاج التراجم ص ٩٥.

الصدر (الشهيد) = الحسام الشهيد.

صدر الشريعة : اشتهر به اثنان أكبر وأصغر. الفوائد ص ٢٤٥

٧١- الصيرفي ؟ لم أستطع تحديد من أراد ، لكنه قبـل سـنة ۸۰۰هـ، حيث نقل عنه الحدادي صاحب الجوهرة النيرة، المتوفى سنة ٨٠٠هـ.

٧٢- الطحاوي أحمد بن محمد أبو جعفر، صاحب المختصر، وشرح معاني الآثار، ت۳۲۱هـ. تاج التراجم ص ١٠٠.

٧٣- الطحطاوي (الطهطاوي) أحمد بن محمد بن إسماعيل، صاحب الحاشية على مراقي الفلاح شرح نور الإيضاح للشرنبلالي

وله حاشية كبيرة على الدر المختار في أربع مجلدات، ت ۱۲۳۱ هـ. الأعلام ٢٤٥/١ ، هدية العارفين ١٨٤/١.

٧٤ - عبد الغني النابلسي بن إسماعيل بن عبد الغني الدمشقي صاحب المؤلفات الكثيرة التي بلغت أكثر من ٢٣٠ مؤلفاً في فنون كثيرة، ت ١١٤٣هـ . هدية العارفين ٥٩٠/١ .

٧٥ - عزمي زاده، مصطفى بن بير محمد المعروف بعزمي زاده، وأيضاً بحالتي الرومي، له حاشية على الدرر والغرر، لمنلا خسرو، وحاشية على الهداية، ونتائج الأفكار على شرح المنار، لابن ملك، ت ١١٤٠ هـ. هدية العارفين ٤٤٠/٢ .

٧٦- العلائي، علاء الدين الحصكفي محمد بن علي، صاحب الدر المختار شرح تنوير الأبصار، وله إفاضة الأنوار على أصول المنار، والدر المنتقى شرح الملتقى ت ١۰۸۸هـ. هدية العارفين .٢٩٥/٢

العمادي = حامد أفندي العمادي.

۷۷- العيني محمود بن أحمد صاحب البناية شرح الهداية، وله مباني الأخبار شرح شرح معاني الآثار، وعمدة القاري شرح صحيح البخاري، ت ٨٥٥هـ . هدية العارفين ٤٢٠/٢ .

۷۸- فخر الإسلام البزدوي علي بن محمد بن الحسين، لـه المبسوط في ۱۱ مجلداً، وشرح الجامع الكبير، والجامع الصغير، وكتاب في أصول الفقه مشهور ، ت ٤٨٢ هـ. ينظـر تـاج التراجم ص ٢٠٥.
Chapter Three: Brief biographies of the notable figures mentioned in al-Lubab

Al-Shumnī: Ahmad bin Kamal al-Din Muhammad bin Muhammad al-Hasan al-Misri Taqi al-Din, the Hanafi jurist. He authored Awfaq al-Masalik li-Ta'diyat al-Manāsik, and 'Ālī al-Rutbah fī Sharh Nazm al-Nukhbah for his father, and Kamāl al-Dirāyah fī Sharh al-Niqāyah, and others. Died 872 AH. Hadiyat al-'Arifīn 1/132. As for his father, he is Kamal al-Din Muhammad bin Muhammad the Maliki jurist, died 821 AH. He authored Nazm Nukhbat al-Fikr fī al-Mustalah by al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar al-'Asqalani. Hadiyat al-'Arifīn 2/183.

69 - Shaykh al-Islam al-Hārithī: Mahmud bin 'Ubayd Allah al-Hārithī al-Marwazī, one of the great imams of the school and disputation. He wrote al-'Awn fī al-Fiqh. Died 606 AH. Al-Fawā'id al-Bahiyyah p. 209.

70 - Author of al-Mujma' in its commentary. It is likely Majma' al-Bahrayn by Muzaffar al-Din ibn al-Sā'ātī Ahmad bin 'Alī. He also wrote al-Badī' fī Usūl al-Fiqh. Died 794 AH. Tāj al-Tarājim p. 95.

Al-Sadr (al-Shahīd) = al-Husām al-Shahīd.

Sadr al-Sharī'ah: Two became famous with this title, the elder and the younger. Al-Fawā'id p. 245.

71 - Al-Sayrafī? I could not determine who he intended, but he was before 800 AH, as al-Haddādī, author of al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, who died 800 AH, transmitted from him.

72 - Al-Tahāwī: Ahmad bin Muhammad Abu Ja'far, author of al-Mukhtasar and Sharh Ma'ānī al-Āthār. Died 321 AH. Tāj al-Tarājim p. 100.

73 - Al-Tahāwī (al-Tahāwī): Ahmad bin Muhammad bin Ismā'īl, author of the gloss on Marāqī al-Falāh Sharh Nūr al-Īdāh by al-Shurunbulālī. He also wrote a large gloss on al-Durr al-Mukhtār in four volumes. Died 1231 AH. Al-A'lām 1/245, Hadiyat al-'Arifīn 1/184.

74 - 'Abd al-Ghanī al-Nābulusī: bin Ismā'īl bin 'Abd al-Ghanī al-Dimashqī, author of numerous works, over 230 in many arts. Died 1143 AH. Hadiyat al-'Arifīn 1/590.

75 - 'Azmī Zādah: Mustafā bin Bīr Muhammad, known as 'Azmī Zādah also as Hālatī al-Rūmī. He wrote a gloss on al-Durar wa al-Ghurar by Mullā Khusraw, a gloss on al-Hidāyah, and Natā'ij al-Afkār on Sharh al-Manār by Ibn Malik. Died 1140 AH. Hadiyat al-'Arifīn 2/440.

76 - Al-'Alā'ī: 'Alā' al-Dīn al-Haskafī Muhammad bin 'Alī, author of al-Durr al-Mukhtār Sharh Tanwīr al-Absār. He also wrote Ifādat al-Anwār 'alā Usūl al-Manār, and al-Durr al-Muntaqā Sharh al-Multaqā. Died 1088 AH. Hadiyat al-'Arifīn 2/295.

Al-'Imādī = Hāmid Afandī al-'Imādī.

77 - Al-'Aynī: Mahmud bin Ahmad, author of al-Bināyah Sharh al-Hidāyah. He also wrote Mabānī al-Akhbār Sharh Sharh Ma'ānī al-Āthār, and 'Umdat al-Qārī Sharh Sahīh al-Bukhārī. Died 855 AH. Hadiyat al-'Arifīn 2/420.

78 - Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawī: 'Alī bin Muhammad bin al-Husayn. He wrote al-Mabsūt in 11 volumes, Sharh al-Jāmi' al-Kabīr, al-Jāmi' al-Saghīr, and a famous book in uṣūl al-fiqh. Died 482 AH. See Tāj al-Tarājim p. 205.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is a biographical appendix from al-Maydani's 'al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri'. It identifies key Hanafi scholars whose names appear in the commentary, providing their full names, notable works, and death dates. The purpose is to help the reader recognize the authority and era of each figure. Notable entries include al-Tahawi (d. 321 AH), whose 'Mukhtasar' is a foundational Hanafi text; al-Haskafi (d. 1088 AH), author of 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar' which is widely relied upon in later fatwa; and al-Bazdawi (d. 482 AH), a major Hanafi usuli scholar. The section also clarifies honorifics like 'Sadr al-Shari'ah' (applied to two scholars) and 'Fakhr al-Islam' (for al-Bazdawi). The textual references (e.g., 'Hadiyat al-'Arifin') show the sources for the biographical data.

Key Terms
صدر الشريعة (Sadr al-Sharī'ah): An honorific title meaning 'Foremost of the Sharia', applied to two Hanafi scholars: the elder (Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar) and the younger (al-Asghar).
فخر الإسلام (Fakhr al-Islam): Honorific meaning 'Pride of Islam', used for 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi, a leading Hanafi usuli scholar.

Life of the Author

Hanafi Scholarly Lineage: Recognizing Key Authorities
Biographical appendix listing Hanafi scholars with their works and death dates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key works and death dates of the Hanafi scholars listed in Lubab and explain their significance in the transmission of Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Know the authors of the mu'tamad texts: Haskafi, Ayni, Bazdawi, and Qutlubugha—your roadmap through Hanafi fiqh.

This lesson introduces you to the Hanafi scholars whose names appear in Al-Lubab. These men are not footnotes; they are the pillars upon which your understanding of Hanafi fiqh rests. By learning their works and dates, you gain the ability to locate any Hanafi ruling in its proper intellectual context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and death date
Read each entry carefully. Note the name (including kunyah and nisbah) and the year of death (t). This helps place the scholar in a historical timeline.
Death dates are crucial for determining whether a scholar is early (mutaqaddimun) or later (mutakhkhirun).
2
Note their most important work and its role in Hanafi fiqh
Each scholar is known for specific works. For example, al-Haskafi wrote al-Durr al-Mukhtar, a key later reference. Identify whether it is a matn, sharh, hashiyah, or fatwa collection.
Match the work to its genre to understand its function in the madhhab.
3
Recognize whether the work is a primary text (matn), commentary (sharh), supercommentary (hashiyah), or fatwa collection
Classify each work. For instance, al-Bazdawi's usul work is a matn on usul, while al-Ayni's al-Binayah is a sharh on al-Hidayah.
Genre affects the level of detail and the audience: matns are concise, shuruhs are expansive.
4
Connect the scholar to the broader Hanafi tradition
Determine if the scholar is from the early (e.g., al-Karkhi, d. 340), middle (e.g., al-Bazdawi, d. 482), or later period (e.g., al-Haskafi, d. 1088). This helps assess the authority of their works.
Later works often serve as the relied-upon (mu'tamad) texts for fatwa.
5
Use the biographical dictionary citations to find more information
Each entry ends with references like 'Hadiyat al-Arifin' or 'Taj al-Tarajim'. These are standard Hanafi biographical sources. Learn to consult them for deeper research.
This skill is essential for verifying chains of transmission and scholarly credibility.

Source Text

الفصل الثالث : ترجمة موجزة للأعلام المذكورين في اللباب

٧٤ - عبد الغني النابلسي بن إسماعيل بن عبد الغني الدمشقي صاحب المؤلفات الكثيرة التي بلغت أكثر من ٢٣٠ مؤلفاً في فنون كثيرة، ت ١١٤٣هـ . هدية العارفين ٥٩٠/١ .

٧٥ - عزمي زاده، مصطفى بن بير محمد المعروف بعزمي زاده، وأيضاً بحالتي الرومي، له حاشية على الدرر والغرر، لمنلا خسرو، وحاشية على الهداية، ونتائج الأفكار على شرح المنار، لابن ملك، ت ١١٤٠ هـ. هدية العارفين ٤٤٠/٢ .

٧٦- العلائي، علاء الدين الحصكفي محمد بن علي، صاحب الدر المختار شرح تنوير الأبصار، وله إفاضة الأنوار على أصول المنار، والدر المنتقى شرح الملتقى ت ١٠۸۸هـ. هدية العارفين ٢٩٥/٢ .

العمادي = حامد أفندي العمادي.

۷۷- العيني محمود بن أحمد صاحب البناية شرح الهداية، وله مباني الأخبار شرح شرح معاني الآثار، وعمدة القاري شرح صحيح البخاري، ت ٨٥٥هـ . هدية العارفين ٤٢٠/٢ .

۷۸- فخر الإسلام البزدوي علي بن محمد بن الحسين، لـه المبسوط في ۱۱ مجلداً، وشرح الجامع الكبير، والجامع الصغير، وكتاب في أصول الفقه مشهور ، ت ٤٨٢ هـ. ينظـر تـاج التراجم ص ٢٠٥.

٧٩ - الفضلي عثمان بن إبراهيم الأسدي المعروف بالفضلي، من فقهاء الحنفية، له فتاوى الفضلي، وهي مشهورة، ت ٥٠٨هـ. ينظر هدية العارفين ٦٥٣/١ ، الجواهر المضية ٥١٥/٢، ٢٧٩/٤.

۸۰ - قاسم بن قطلوبغا زين الدين الجمالي، صاحب تصحيح القدوري، وتاج التراجم هدية العارفين ٨٣٠/١.

۸۱ - القاضي أبو علي النسفي عبد العزيز بن عثمان بن إبراهيم بن محمد الفضلي النسفي القاضي، له كتاب الفحول في علم الأصول، ت ٥٣٣هـ. تاج التراجم ص ۱۹۰ ، الجواهر المضية ٤٣١/٢ .

۸۲ - القهستاني شمس الدين محمد بن حسام الدين البخاري، صاحب جامع الرموز في شرح النقاية وجامع المباني في شرح فقه الكيداني، ت ٩٦٢هـ . هدية العارفين ٢٤٤/٢

۸۳- الكرخي أبو الحسن عبيد الله بن الحسن، لـه مختصر الكرخي في فروع الحنفية، والجامع الكبير، والجامع الصغير، ت ٣٤٠هـ. تاج التراجم ص ٢٠٠.

۸۴- الكردري : لعله عبد الغفور بن لقمـان تـاج الـديـن أبـو المفاخر، تولى قضاء حلب لنور الدين محمود الزنكي، له شرح على التجريد في فروع الحنفية للكرماني، سماه المفيد والمزيد، وله شرح على الجامع الصغير ، ت ٥٥٢هـ ، تاج التراجم ص ١٩٤.
Chapter Three: Brief Biographies of the Notable Figures Mentioned in Lubab

74 - Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulsi, son of Isma'il, son of Abd al-Ghani al-Dimashqi, author of many works, exceeding 230 in various arts, died 1143 AH. Hadiyat al-Arifin 1/590.

75 - Azmi Zada, Mustafa ibn Bir Muhammad, known as Azmi Zada and also as Halati al-Rumi. He has a supercommentary on al-Durar wa al-Ghirar of Mulla Khusrau, and a supercommentary on al-Hidayah, and Nata'ij al-Afkar on Sharh al-Manar of Ibn Malik, died 1140 AH. Hadiyat al-Arifin 2/440.

76 - Al-Alai, Ala al-Din al-Haskafi Muhammad ibn Ali, author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar Sharh Tanwir al-Absar, and Ifadat al-Anwar on Usul al-Manar, and al-Durr al-Muntaqa Sharh al-Multaqa, died 1088 AH. Hadiyat al-Arifin 2/295.

Al-Imadi = Hamid Afandi al-Imadi.

77 - Al-Ayni Mahmud ibn Ahmad, author of al-Binayah Sharh al-Hidayah, and Mabani al-Akhbar Sharh Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar, and Umdat al-Qari Sharh Sahih al-Bukhari, died 855 AH. Hadiyat al-Arifin 2/420.

78 - Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi Ali ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn, author of al-Mabsut in 11 volumes, and commentary on al-Jami al-Kabir, and al-Jami al-Saghir, and a famous book on usul al-fiqh, died 482 AH. See Taj al-Tarajim p. 205.

79 - Al-Fadali Uthman ibn Ibrahim al-Asadi known as al-Fadali, a Hanafi jurist, author of Fatawa al-Fadali, which is famous, died 508 AH. See Hadiyat al-Arifin 1/653, al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya 2/515, 4/279.

80 - Qasim ibn Qutlubugha Zain al-Din al-Jamali, author of Tashih al-Quduri and Taj al-Tarajim. Hadiyat al-Arifin 1/830.

81 - Al-Qadi Abu Ali al-Nasafi Abd al-Aziz ibn Uthman ibn Ibrahim ibn Muhammad al-Fadali al-Nasafi al-Qadi, author of Kitab al-Fuhul fi Ilm al-Usul, died 533 AH. Taj al-Tarajim p. 190, al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya 2/431.

82 - Al-Qahistani Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Husam al-Din al-Bukhari, author of Jami al-Rumuz fi Sharh al-Niqayah and Jami al-Mabani fi Sharh Fiqh al-Kaydani, died 962 AH. Hadiyat al-Arifin 2/244.

83 - Al-Karkhi Abu al-Hasan Ubayd Allah ibn al-Hasan, author of Mukhtasar al-Karkhi in Hanafi furu, and al-Jami al-Kabir, and al-Jami al-Saghir, died 340 AH. Taj al-Tarajim p. 200.

84 - Al-Kardari: perhaps Abd al-Ghafur ibn Luqman Taj al-Din Abu al-Mafakhir, who served as judge of Aleppo for Nur al-Din Mahmud al-Zinki. He has a commentary on al-Tajrid fi Furu al-Hanafiyyah of al-Karmani, named al-Mufid wa al-Mazid, and a commentary on al-Jami al-Saghir, died 552 AH. Taj al-Tarajim p. 194.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is a biographical appendix from Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri by Al-Maydani. It provides brief notices of key Hanafi scholars whose names appear in the main text, serving as a valuable reference for readers to understand the chain of authority and scholarly lineage. Each entry typically includes the scholar's full name, notable works, and death date, followed by a citation to biographical dictionaries like Hadiyat al-Arifin and Taj al-Tarajim. The section covers 11 scholars: (74) Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulsi, a prolific Damascene author; (75) Azmi Zada, known for supercommentaries; (76) Al-Haskafi, author of Durr al-Mukhtar (a foundational work in later Hanafi fatwa); (77) Al-Ayni, famous for his commentary on Sahih al-Bukhari (Umdat al-Qari) and on Hidayah (Al-Binayah); (78) Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, an early Hanafi master whose works on usul (Kanz al-Wusul) are central; (79) Al-Fadali, known for his fatwa collection; (80) Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, editor of Al-Quduri's text; (81) Al-Nasafi, a judge and usul scholar; (82) Al-Qahistani, commentator on fiqh works; (83) Al-Karkhi, an early authority whose mukhtasar is important; (84) Al-Kardari, a Hanafi judge and commentator. This list helps the student appreciate the depth and continuity of the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
حاشية (hāshiyah): A supercommentary or marginal annotation on a main text; in this passage, it refers to works like 'Hāshiyah ʻalā al-Durar wa al-Ghirar'.
الدر المختار (al-Durr al-Mukhtār): A famous Hanafi fiqh work by al-Haskafi, a commentary on Tanwīr al-Abṣār; it is a key reference for later fatwa.
تصحيح (taṣḥīḥ): The act of correcting or verifying a text; here, 'Taṣḥīḥ al-Qudūrī' refers to the critical edition of al-Qudūrī's Mukhtasar.

Key Takeaway
Knowing the scholars and their works is essential for understanding the authority and chain of transmission of Hanafi fiqh.

Life of the Author
beginner
10 min
Key Hanafi Jurists in al-Lubab
Biographical appendix of Hanafi scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major Hanafi jurists mentioned in al-Lubab and state their most significant works and contributions to the madhhab.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school's authority rests on a chain of scholars from the 2nd to 9th centuries AH, each building on the previous generation's work.

Al-Lubab concludes with a biographical appendix that lists the scholars cited throughout the text. This section is not merely a list of names; it is a scholarly pedigree that shows the transmission of knowledge from Imam Abu Hanifa through his students and subsequent commentators. Knowing who these scholars are and when they lived helps you understand the weight of their opinions and the chain of authority in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the earliest scholars
Look for the death dates (ت) and find the earliest, such as Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani (d. 189 AH) and Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi (d. 242 AH). These are the direct students of Abu Hanifa and his immediate successors.
Al-Shaybani's works al-Asl, al-Jami' al-Kabir, and al-Jami' al-Saghir form the core of Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the later commentators and compilers
Note scholars from the 5th to 9th centuries, such as al-Fadli (d. 508 AH), al-Kardari (d. 552 AH), and Ibn al-Humam (d. 861 AH). These scholars wrote commentaries, corrections, and fatwa collections that refined and transmitted the madhhab.
Ibn al-Humam's Fath al-Qadir is a key commentary on al-Hidayah.
3
Recognize patterns in titles and roles
Observe titles like 'Burhan al-A'immah' (al-Mahbubi) and 'Taj al-Shari'a' (Mahmud al-Mahbubi). Also note roles such as 'al-Qadi' (judge) and 'Shams al-A'immah'. These indicate the scholar's rank and specialization.
The title often reflects the scholar's contribution to proof-based reasoning (Burhan) or to legal theory (Taj al-Shari'a).
4
Connect scholars to their major works
Match each scholar to the work(s) mentioned. For example, al-Qahistani authored Jami' al-Rumuz, al-Karkhi wrote Mukhtasar al-Karkhi, and al-Kamal Ibn al-Humam wrote Fath al-Qadir and al-Tahrir.
Many of these works are still studied in the Hanafi curriculum today.
5
Understand the source of authority
Realize that these scholars are not just names; their works are the foundation for Hanafi fatwa. The references to Hadiyyat al-Arifin and al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya show that the compiler is verifying the scholarly pedigree.
The chain: Abu Hanifa -> Muhammad al-Shaybani -> later mujtahids -> commentators -> muftis.

Chapter Three: A Brief Translation of the Scholars Mentioned in al-Lubab
79 - al-Fadli: Uthman ibn Ibrahim al-Asadi known as al-Fadli, from the Hanafi jurists, he has Fatawa al-Fadli, which are famous, d. 508 AH. See Hadiyyat al-Arifin 1/653, al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya 2/515, 4/279.
Qasim ibn Qutlubagha Zayn al-Din al-Jamali, author of Tashih al-Quduri, and Taj al-Tarajim Hadiyyat al-Arifin 1/830.
Al-Qadi Abu Ali al-Nasafi: Abd al-Aziz ibn Uthman ibn Ibrahim ibn Muhammad al-Fadli al-Nasafi al-Qadi, he has the book al-Fuhul fi Ilm al-Usul, d. 533 AH. Taj al-Tarajim p. 190, al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya 2/431.
Qadi Khan = al-Uzjandi. Al-Qadi, perhaps al-Qadi Abu Ali al-Nasafi = al-Qadi Abu Ali al-Nasafi, or the intended is Qadi Khan = al-Hasan ibn Mansur.
82 - al-Qahistani: Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Husam al-Din al-Bukhari, author of Jami' al-Rumuz fi Sharh al-Nuqaya and Jami' al-Mabani fi Sharh Fiqh al-Kaydani, d. 962 AH. Hadiyyat al-Arifin 2/244.
83 - al-Karkhi: Abu al-Hasan Ubayd Allah ibn al-Hasan, he has Mukhtasar al-Karkhi in Hanafi furu', and al-Jami' al-Kabir, and al-Jami' al-Saghir, d. 340 AH. Taj al-Tarajim p. 200.
84 - al-Kardari: perhaps Abd al-Ghafur ibn Luqman Taj al-Din Abu al-Mafakhir, he was judge of Aleppo for Nur al-Din Mahmud al-Zanki, he has a commentary on al-Tajrid in Hanafi furu' by al-Kirmani, called al-Mufid wa al-Mazid, and a commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir, d. 552 AH, Taj al-Tarajim p. 194.
Or the intended is: Muhammad ibn Abd al-Sattar al-Kardari, known as Shams al-A'immah, student of the author of al-Hidaya, he has a commentary on al-Ikhsiti in usul (al-Muntakhab), d. 642 AH. Taj al-Tarajim p. 267.
85 - al-Kamal Ibn al-Humam: Muhammad ibn Abd al-Wahid al-Siwasi, author of Fath al-Qadir li al-Ajiz al-Faqir Sharh al-Hidaya, and author of al-Tahrir fi Usul al-Fiqh, d. 861 AH. al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya pp. 17, 180.
Al-Mahbubi: Burhan al-A'immah al-Mahbubi = Burhan al-A'immah. Or the intended: Mahmud ibn Ubayd Allah ibn Mahmud al-Mahbubi Taj al-Shari'a al-Mahbubi, he has Mukhtasar al-Hidaya al-Wiqaya Taj al-Tarajim p. 291.
Muhammad ibn Hamid: perhaps al-Artahi, d. before 600 AH, or the intended: al-Bayyi', d. 623 AH, as there are more than one Muhammad ibn Hamid. al-Jawahir 3/113.
87 - Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani: student of Imam Abu Hanifa, he has the book al-Asl (al-Mabsut), al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Jami' al-Saghir, and others, d. 189 AH. Taj al-Tarajim p. 237.
Muhammad ibn Shuja' al-Thalji = al-Thalji.
88 - Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Najjari al-Kamari, he was a great imam, reliable in narration, a scholar in knowledge, and the famous books of fatawa are filled with his fatawa and narrations, d. 381 AH. al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 184.
89 - Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi: from the companions of Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, he has the book al-Muda'a wa al-Muda'a Alayh, d. 242 AH. al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p., Tahdhib al-Tahdhib 9/469, Hadiyyat al-Arifin 2/13.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical compilation from the end of al-Lubab, providing brief identifications of the scholars whose names appear in the main text. It is a reference section (الفصل الثالث: ترجمة موجزة للأعلام المذكورين في اللباب) meant to help readers recognize the authorities quoted. The entries include well-known Hanafi jurists such as al-Fadli (d. 508 AH), author of Fatawa al-Fadli; Qasim ibn Qutlubagha (d. ?) who wrote a correction of al-Quduri; and al-Qadi Abu Ali al-Nasafi (d. 533 AH) who authored al-Fuhul fi Usul. The passage also mentions Qadi Khan (al-Hasan ibn Mansur), a major Hanafi authority; al-Qahistani (d. 962 AH) commentator on al-Nuqaya; al-Karkhi (d. 340 AH) a foundational Hanafi scholar; al-Kardari (d. 552 AH or 642 AH) with two possible identifications; Ibn al-Humam (d. 861 AH) the great Hanafi jurist and usuli; al-Mahbubi (Taj al-Shari'a); and the famous students of Abu Hanifa such as Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani (d. 189 AH). It also notes Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi (d. 242 AH) a companion of al-Shaybani. The compiler often gives death dates (ت) and references to biographical dictionaries like Hadiyyat al-Arifin and al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya. This section underscores the rich scholarly tradition of the Hanafi school and the reliance on authoritative figures whose works form the backbone of Hanafi fiqh and usul.

Key Terms
برهان الأئمة (Burhan al-A'immah): A title meaning 'Proof of the Imams', used for a Hanafi scholar (al-Mahbubi) as per the text.
تاج الشريعة (Taj al-Shari'ah): A title meaning 'Crown of the Law', used for Mahmud ibn Ubayd Allah al-Mahbubi in the text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school is preserved through a chain of authoritative scholars; knowing their names and works is essential for understanding the weight of their opinions.

Life of the Author

Biography of Shams al-A'imma al-Kardari
Biographical identification of a Hanafi scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Shams al-A'imma al-Kardari by his full name, teacher, work, and death date.

Core Idea
Shams al-A'imma al-Kardari: student of al-Marghinani and commentator on al-Ikhsikti's usul.

This lesson introduces Muhammad ibn Abd al-Sattar al-Kardari, known as Shams al-A'imma, a distinguished Hanafi scholar who studied under the author of al-Hidayah and authored a commentary on al-Ikhsikti's al-Muntakhab in usul al-fiqh. Knowing his biography helps trace later Hanafi scholarly chains.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's name and honorific
Locate the full name (Muhammad ibn Abd al-Sattar al-Kardari) and his title (Shams al-A'imma). Memorize both as they appear in Hanafi biographical sources.
The title 'Shams al-A'imma' is also used for other scholars, so specify al-Kardari when referring to this individual.
2
Note his teacher and major work
Identify that his teacher is the author of al-Hidayah (Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani). His main work is a commentary on al-Ikhsikti's usul text, titled al-Muntakhab.

Al-Kamal ibn al-Hammam: His Life and Works
Biographical note on a key Hanafi scholar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the full name, key works, and death year of al-Kamal ibn al-Hammam and identify why he is significant in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Al-Kamal ibn al-Hammam authored Fath al-Qadir and al-Tahrir, two pillars of later Hanafi fiqh and usul.

Al-Kamal ibn al-Hammam is a towering figure in the Hanafi school. His commentary on al-Hidayah, Fath al-Qadir, became a standard reference for later scholars. His usul work, al-Tahrir, is a foundational text in Hanafi legal theory. This lesson introduces you to his identity and his lasting contributions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and kunya.
The text gives: al-Kamal ibn al-Hammam Muhammad ibn Abd al-Wahid al-Siwasi. Note the kunya 'Ibn al-Hammam' and the nisba 'al-Siwasi' indicating origin from Siwas.
2
Recognize his major works in fiqh and usul.
He authored Fath al-Qadir, a commentary on al-Hidayah (fiqh), and al-Tahrir in usul al-fiqh. These are two distinct disciplines.
3
Note his death year and its significance.
He died in 861 AH. This places him in the 9th century AH, a period of rich Hanafi scholarship and commentary activity.
4
Understand the role of Fath al-Qadir in Hanafi fiqh.
Fath al-Qadir is a comprehensive sharh (commentary) on al-Hidayah by Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani. It is widely cited by late Hanafi jurists for its depth and resolution of ikhtilaf.
5
Connect al-Tahrir's status in usul al-fiqh.
Al-Tahrir became a standard textbook for Hanafi usul, often memorized and commented upon by later scholars like Ibn Abidin and al-Babarti.

Biographical entry listing works and date of death

Learning Objective

Core Idea
al-Shaybani authored the six canonical works that form the backbone of the Hanafi school.

This lesson introduces you to Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, the foremost student of Abu Hanifa. He did not just preserve his teacher's rulings; he compiled, systematised, and transmitted them into the six works known collectively as Zahir al-Riwayah. Understanding his biography and works is essential for navigating Hanafi fiqh texts.

Guided Path

The passage mentions three works by name: al-Asl (also known as al-Mabsut), al-Jami' al-Kabir, and al-Jami' al-Saghir. Know that these are part of a set of six works (Zahir al-Riwayah).
The other three are al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, and al-Ziyadat.

189 AH is given. This places al-Shaybani's death roughly two decades after Abu Hanifa (150 AH). It helps contextualise the timeline of the school's development.

Biographical entry for a student of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani

By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi as a student of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and state his major work al-Mudda‘a wa al-Mudda‘a ‘alayh.

Core Idea
Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi authored al-Mudda‘a wa al-Mudda‘a ‘alayh, a core Hanafi text on judicial procedure.

In the transmission of Hanafi fiqh, the students of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani played a crucial role. This lesson introduces one such scholar, Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi, who preserved and systematized Hanafi teachings on judicial procedure. Knowing his place in the chain of narrators helps us assess the reliability of his transmitted rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's name and lineage
Notice the name: Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi. The attributive 'al-Razi' indicates he was from Rayy, a city in Iran.

Identify the teacher

3
Identify the student's work
He authored the book al-Mudda‘a wa al-Mudda‘a ‘alayh, meaning 'The Plaintiff and the Defendant', which deals with judicial procedure and evidence in Hanafi fiqh.

4
Note the death date
He died in 242 AH, which places him in the early third century after the Hijrah.
This helps establish his generation and transmission chain.
5
Place him in the Hanafi transmission chain
As a direct student of Shaybani, he is part of the third generation of Hanafi scholars after Abu Hanifa (first generation: Abu Hanifa; second: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad; third: their students).
His work is part of the Nawādir (rare transmissions) but still respected.

Knowing the lives of our scholars strengthens our connection to the madhhab. This lesson introduces you to Mulla Ali al-Turkmani, a chief judge and a defender of Hanafi fiqh, whose work al-Jawhar al-Naqi remains a notable source for understanding Hanafi positions against objections.

This work is considered an important source for Hanafi polemics.

He died in 750 AH. Memorize this to place him in the timeline of Hanafi scholarship.

Al-Natif: Author of al-Waqi'at
Biographical entry for the author of al-Waqi'at

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify al-Natif and state his major works and their significance in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Al-Natif's al-Waqi'at documents actual legal cases, anchoring Hanafi practice in real-life rulings.

Al-Natif was a 5th-century Hanafi jurist whose works preserved the practical application of the madhhab. His collection of waqi'at (real cases) and his text on legal categories provide essential resources for understanding Hanafi furu' and qawa'id.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar
Read the full name: Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Umar Abu al-Abbas, known as al-Natif. Note his kunya and nisba.
Al-Natif is a nisba indicating he was from a place called Natif or associated with it.
2
Note the death date
He died in 446 AH (approximately 1054 CE). This places him in the 5th century of Islam.
This period is after the great Hanafi imams but before later authoritative works like al-Hidayah.
3
Identify his major work
He is called 'sahib al-Waqi'at' – the author of al-Waqi'at, a collection of actual legal cases (waqi'at) in Hanafi furu'.
Waqi'at are real-occurring cases, not hypothetical, making them crucial for fatwa.
4
Identify his other work
He also authored al-Ajnas wa al-Furuq, a work on legal categories (ajnas) and distinctions (furuq), used in usul and qawa'id.
This work helps in applying legal maxims and distinguishing similar cases.
5
Understand significance
Both works are important references for later Hanafi scholars. Al-Waqi'at provides practical rulings; al-Ajnas wa al-Furuq aids in legal reasoning.
These texts are part of the nawadir (rare transmissions) that complement the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الناطفي أحمد بن محمد بن عمر أبو العباس، صاحب الواقعات في فروع الحنفية، وله الأجناس والفروق، ت ٤٤٦هـ.
al-Natif: Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Umar Abu al-Abbas, author of al-Waqi'at in Hanafi furu', and he has al-Ajnas wa al-Furuq, died 446 AH.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This entry introduces al-Natif, Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Hanafi. He authored al-Waqi'at, a collection of actual legal cases (waqi'at) in Hanafi fiqh, and also wrote al-Ajnas wa al-Furuq (Types and Distinctions), a work on legal maxims. He died in 446 AH.

Key Terms
الواقعات (al-Waqi'at): A collection of real-life legal cases and rulings.
الأجناس والفروق (al-Ajnas wa al-Furuq): A work on legal categories and distinctions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) al-Waqi'at
C) Kanz al-Daqa'iq
D) al-Hidayah

Key Takeaway
Al-Natif authored al-Waqi'at, a foundational collection of Hanafi cases, and al-Ajnas wa al-Furuq on legal distinctions.

Distinguishing Two Scholars: Najm al-A'imma al-Bukhari and al-Hakimi
Biographical note on two Hanafi scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi scholars titled Najm al-A'imma and state why distinguishing them is important in Hanafi biographical studies.

Core Idea
Two Hanafi scholars share the title Najm al-A'imma; knowing which is which prevents confusion in chains of transmission.

In Hanafi biographical literature, titles like 'Najm al-A'imma' can be shared by multiple scholars. This lesson clarifies that al-Lakhnawi recorded two such scholars—one a teacher of a famous jurist, the other a student of Qadi Khan. Understanding their identities helps in accurately attributing works and tracing scholarly chains.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source
The passage cites al-Lakhnawi’s al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya, a key biographical dictionary for Hanafi scholars. Recognize that this is a standard reference for verifying scholar identities.
Al-Lakhnawi (d. 1304 AH) compiled biographies of Hanafi jurists.
2
Note the shared laqab
The title 'Najm al-A'imma' (Star of the Imams) is shared by two scholars. Mark this as a potential point of confusion.
Laqab (honorific title) can be duplicated across generations.
3
Distinguish by association
The first is Najm al-A'imma al-Bukhari, teacher of Fakhr al-Din al-Badi' al-Qazwini. The second is Najm al-A'imma al-Hakimi, student of Qadi Khan. These relationships help differentiate them.
Fakhr al-Din al-Badi' al-Qazwini was a Hanafi jurist; Qadi Khan is the author of al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya.
4
Recognize the lacuna
Al-Lakhnawi noted that neither scholar is known to have authored works. This informs us that their legacy is through teaching, not writing.
This explains why they are less prominent in later Hanafi literature.
5
Apply awareness
When encountering the title 'Najm al-A'imma' in a text, verify which scholar is intended by checking context (teacher/student or regional association).
This practice prevents misattribution in academic work.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نجم الأئمة في شرحه، ذكر اللكنوي في الفوائد البهية ص ٢٢٠ اثنين بهذا اللقب : نجم الأئمة البخاري أستاذ فخر الدين البديع القزويني ونجم الأئمة الحكيمي تلميذ قاضي خان، ولم يذكر لهما مصنفات
Najm al-A'imma in his commentary; al-Lakhnawi mentioned in al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p.220 two with this title: Najm al-A'imma al-Bukhari, teacher of Fakhr al-Din al-Badi' al-Qazwini, and Najm al-A'imma al-Hakimi, student of Qadi Khan, and he did not mention any authored works for them.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This entry is a note from the commentator (possibly the author of Lubab al-Sharh) citing al-Lakhnawi's al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya. It clarifies that there are two Hanafi scholars both known as 'Najm al-A'imma': al-Bukhari (teacher of Fakhr al-Din al-Badi' al-Qazwini) and al-Hakimi (student of Qadi Khan). Al-Lakhnawi noted that neither is known to have authored works.

Key Terms
الفوائد البهية (al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya): Biographical work on Hanafi scholars by al-Lakhnawi.
نجم الأئمة (Najm al-A'imma): Honorific title meaning 'Star of the Imams', shared by at least two Hanafi scholars.
البخاري (al-Bukhari): the one from Bukhara; here refers to Najm al-A'imma al-Bukhari, teacher of Fakhr al-Din al-Badi' al-Qazwini.
الحكيمي (al-Hakimi): the one from Hakim?; here refers to Najm al-A'imma al-Hakimi, student of Qadi Khan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Lakhnawi records two Hanafi scholars named Najm al-A'imma—al-Bukhari and al-Hakimi—neither of whom authored known works; this prevents misattribution in Hanafi studies.

The entry ends mid-sentence. This is a reminder that manuscript sources often have gaps; cross-referencing with other works is necessary.

Biographical Appendix: Scholars Cited in Al-Lubab
Biographical reference appendix

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi scholars cited in Al-Lubab and distinguish them from the Shafi'i scholar al-Nawawi based on their works and affiliations.

Core Idea
Know the scholars — their madhhab and key works — to correctly attribute rulings in the commentary.

This appendix is a reference tool, not a source of fiqh rulings. It lists scholars mentioned in the commentary Al-Lubab, providing death dates, major works, and madhhab affiliations. Most are Hanafi, but al-Nawawi (a Shafi'i) is included because his works are widely referenced. Understanding who these scholars are helps you evaluate the authority behind citations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's name and epithet
Each entry begins with a name often accompanied by a title or nickname (e.g., 'Miskin', 'al-Natifi'). Note the full name and any honorific.
Some entries have cross-references to other entries.
2
Determine the death date (t)
The death date (given as 't' followed by AH year) places the scholar chronologically and helps assess contemporary influence.
Dates are approximate; 't 954' means died 954 AH.
3
Identify key works
Each scholar's major writings are listed (e.g., 'Sharh Kanz al-Daqa'iq', 'al-Waqi'at'). These indicate their expertise and contributions.
Works may be commentaries, fatwa collections, or usul texts.
4
Note the madhhab affiliation
Most are Hanafi, but the appendix explicitly marks al-Nawawi as Shafi'i. For others, their works or titles (e.g., 'al-Hanafi') confirm affiliation.
Al-Nawawi's inclusion shows cross-madhhab reliance.
5
Check bibliographical sources
References like Hadiyat al-'Arifin and Taj al-Tarajim are given. Recognizing these sources helps you locate further information.
These are standard Hanafi biographical dictionaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث: ترجمة موجزة للأعلام المذكورين في اللباب

۹۰- مسكين هو معين الدين محمد بن عبد الله الهروي، المعروف بمنلا مسكين له شرح على كنز الدقائق، وعليه حاشية لأبي السعود، ت ٩٥٤هـ. هدية العارفين ٢٤٢/٢.

۹۱ - منلا علي التركماني، لعله غالباً علاء الدين علي بن عثمان ابن إبراهيم المارديني ثم المصري، قاضي القضاة، المعروف بابن التركماني، صاحب الجوهر النقي في الرد على البيهقي، ت ٧٥٠هـ، ينظر هدية العارفين ٧٢٠/١.
منلا مسكين = مسكين.
الموصلي = أبو الفضل الموصلي.

٩٢ - الناطفي أحمد بن محمد بن عمر أبو العباس، صاحب الواقعات في فروع الحنفية، وله الأجناس والفروق، ت ٤٤٦هـ. هدية العارفين ٧٦/١ ، تاج التراجم ص ١٠٢.

۹۳ - نجم الأئمة الحفصي طاهر بن محمد بن عمرو أبو المعالي الحفصي، له الفصول في علم الأصول، ت في حدود سنة ٦٢٠هـ. هدية العارفين ٤٣٠/١ ، تاج التراجم ص ۱۷۳.

٩٤ - نجم الأئمة في شرحه، ذكر اللكنوي في الفوائد البهية ص ۲۲۰ اثنين بهذا اللقب: نجم الأئمة البخاري أستاذ فخر الدين البديع القزويني ونجم الأئمة الحكيمي تلميذ قاضي خان، ولم يذكر لهما مصنفات، الجواهر المضية ٤٤٠/٤، ١٨٢/٤، وينظر نجم الأئمة البارعي المتوفى سنة ٦٤٥هـ في الجواهر المضية ١٤٤/٤. النسفي = أبو البركات حافظ الدين.

٩٥ - نوح أفندي، نوح بن مصطفى أفندي القونوي، له حاشية على الدرر والغرر، وكتب كثيرة أخرى، ت ١٠٧٠هـ. هدية العارفين ٤٩٨/٢.

٩٦ - النووي يحيى بن شرف الإمام المحدث الفقيه الشافعي المشهور، صاحب المصنفات المشهورة: رياض الصالحين، والمجموع، وشرح صحيح مسلم، ت ٦٧٦هـ. هدية العارفين ٥٢٤/٢.

۹۷ - هشام بن عبيد الله الرازي تلميذ الصاحبين، ت ٢٢١هـ، الجواهر المضية ٥٦٩/٣ ، تذكرة الحفاظ ٣٨٧/١.

۹۸ - هلال الرازي بن يحيى بن مسلم، ويقال له: هلال الرازي، وهلال الرأي، كما في البناية ٦٢٨/٩ (ط باكستان)، وقيل له هلال الرأي؛ لسعة علمه، كما قيل لربيعة الرأي شيخ الإمام مالك، وهلال تلميذ أبي يوسف وزفر صاحبي الإمام أبي حنيفة، له مصنف الشروط، وله أحكام الوقف، ت ٢٤٥هـ. تاج التراجم ص ٣١٢.

٩٩ - الواني محمد بن مصطفى الكوراني الرومي الحنفي، المعروف بالواني، تولى قضاء المدينة المنورة، وتوفي بها سنة ١٠٠٠هـ، له عدة تأليف منها ترجيح البينات، وحاشية على شرح السيد للفرائض للسجاوندي. هدية العارفين ٢٦٠/٢. وهناك أكثر من علم لقبه: (الواني)، وهذا هو الفقيه الحنفي منهم، وهو المراد، والله أعلم.

١٠٠ - الولوالجي عبد الرشيد بن أبي حنيفة نعمان الـولوالجي ظهير الدين، له الأمالي في الفقه والفتاوى، ت ٥٤٠هـ. هدية العارفين ٥٦٨/١ ، الفوائد البهية ص ٩٤.
Chapter Three: Brief Biography of the Notables Mentioned in Al-Lubab

90 - Miskin is Mu'in al-Din Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah al-Harawi, known as Mulla Miskin. He has a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, and there is a gloss on it by Abu al-Su'ud. Died 954 AH. (Hadiyat al-'Arifin 2/242)

91 - Mulla 'Ali al-Turkumani, likely 'Ala' al-Din 'Ali ibn 'Uthman ibn Ibrahim al-Mardini then al-Misri, chief judge, known as Ibn al-Turkumani, author of al-Jawhar al-Naqi fi al-Radd 'ala al-Bayhaqi. Died 750 AH. (See Hadiyat al-'Arifin 1/720)
Mulla Miskin = Miskin.
Al-Mawsili = Abu al-Fadl al-Mawsili.

92 - Al-Natifi Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn 'Umar Abu al-'Abbas, author of al-Waqi'at fi Furu' al-Hanafiyyah, and he has al-Ajnas wa al-Furuq. Died 446 AH. (Hadiyat al-'Arifin 1/76, Taj al-Tarajim p. 102)

93 - Najm al-A'immah al-Hafsi Tahir ibn Muhammad ibn 'Amr Abu al-Ma'ali al-Hafsi. He has al-Fusul fi 'Ilm al-Usul. Died around 620 AH. (Hadiyat al-'Arifin 1/430, Taj al-Tarajim p. 173)

94 - Najm al-A'immah in his commentary. Al-Laknawi mentioned in al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah (p. 220) two with this epithet: Najm al-A'immah al-Bukhari, teacher of Fakhr al-Din al-Bad' al-Qazwini, and Najm al-A'immah al-Hakimi, student of Qadi Khan. He did not mention any works for them. (Al-Jawahir al-Madiyyah 4/440, 4/182) And see Najm al-A'immah al-Bari' who died 645 AH in al-Jawahir al-Madiyyah 4/144. Al-Nasafi = Abu al-Barakat Hafiz al-Din.

95 - Nuh Afandi, Nuh ibn Mustafa Afandi al-Qunawi. He has a gloss on al-Durar wa al-Ghurur, and many other books. Died 1070 AH. (Hadiyat al-'Arifin 2/498)

96 - Al-Nawawi, Yahya ibn Sharaf, the well-known hadith scholar and Shafi'i jurist, author of famous works: Riyad al-Salihin, al-Majmu', and Sharh Sahih Muslim. Died 676 AH. (Hadiyat al-'Arifin 2/524)

97 - Hisham ibn 'Ubayd Allah al-Razi, student of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Died 221 AH. (Al-Jawahir al-Madiyyah 3/569, Tadhkirat al-Huffaz 1/387)

98 - Hilal al-Razi ibn Yahya ibn Muslim. He is called Hilal al-Razi, and Hilal al-Ra'y, as in al-Binayah 9/628 (Pakistan ed.). He was called Hilal al-Ra'y due to the breadth of his knowledge, just as Rabi'ah al-Ra'y, the teacher of Imam Malik, was called. Hilal was a student of Abu Yusuf and Zufar, the two companions of Imam Abu Hanifah. He has a work on conditions (al-Shurut) and a book on rulings of waqf. Died 245 AH. (Taj al-Tarajim p. 312)

99 - Al-Wani, Muhammad ibn Mustafa al-Kurani al-Rumi al-Hanafi, known as al-Wani. He served as judge of Medina and died there in 1000 AH. He has several works, including Tarjih al-Bayyinat and a gloss on al-Sayyid's commentary on al-Fara'id for al-Sajawandi. (Hadiyat al-'Arifin 2/260) There are more than one scholar with the title (al-Wani), and this one is the Hanafi jurist among them, and he is the intended one. And Allah knows best.

100 - Al-Walwaliji, 'Abd al-Rashid ibn Abi Hanifah Nu'man al-Walwaliji, Zahir al-Din. He has al-Amali fi al-Fiqh wa al-Fatawa. Died 540 AH. (Hadiyat al-'Arifin 1/568, al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah p. 94)
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is a biographical appendix to the commentary Al-Lubab, listing scholars cited in the work. It is not a fiqh ruling but rather a reference tool. The appendix provides death dates (t) and key works for each scholar, as well as cross-references to biographical sources like Hadiyat al-'Arifin, Taj al-Tarajim, and al-Jawahir al-Madiyyah. Most scholars are Hanafi jurists, but note that al-Nawawi (entry 96) is a Shafi'i scholar, included because his works are widely used. The entry for Hilal al-Razi (98) clarifies his epithet 'al-Ra'y' (opinion) due to his vast knowledge, analogous to Rabi'ah al-Ra'y. The appendix aims to help readers identify the authorities behind the rulings discussed in the main text. The teacher should emphasize that this section is for orientation, not substantive law.

Key Terms
هدية العارفين (Hadiyat al-'Arifin): A biographical dictionary by Isma'il Pasha al-Baghdadi, used as a source for death dates and works.
تاج التراجم (Taj al-Tarajim): A biographical work by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha al-Hanafi, focusing on Hanafi scholars.
الفقيه الحنفي (al-faqih al-Hanafi): A jurist who follows the Hanafi school of law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

This appendix equips you to identify the madhhab, period, and key works of scholars cited in Al-Lubab, a crucial skill for contextualizing fiqh authorities.

Biography of Imam al-Quduri
Introduces the biographical chapter on al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of Imam al-Quduri and explain his significance as the author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational text in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Imam al-Quduri authored the foundational Mukhtasar, a key matn in Hanafi fiqh.

This passage opens the biographical chapter on Imam al-Quduri, the author of the Mukhtasar (concise manual) that this commentary explains. Knowing the author's background—his full name, dates, and scholarly titles—helps us appreciate the authority of the matn and the chain of transmission. This tarjamah is a standard feature in classical fiqh works, reminding the reader of the human chain behind the rulings.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the structure of a tarjamah
Notice that this passage is not a legal ruling but a biographical introduction. It begins with honorific titles and then gives the full name and dates.
Tarjamah sections are common at the start of commentaries to establish the author's authority.
2
Extract key biographical data
Identify the full name: Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri. Note his birth (362 AH) and death (428 AH) years, and the supplication for mercy.
The dates anchor the scholar in the timeline of Hanafi scholarship.
3
Understand the honorific titles
The titles 'al-imam', 'al-faqih', and 'al-muhaddith' indicate that al-Quduri was a leading authority, a jurist, and a hadith scholar, respectively.
These titles reflect the high esteem in which he was held and his comprehensive expertise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

رحمه الله تعالى :
The First Chapter: A biography of the Imam, the jurist, the hadith scholar, Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (362 AH – 428 AH), may Allah have mercy on him:
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This is a standard opening for a biographical section in a classical fiqh commentary. The author, al-Quduri, is the writer of the Matn (al-Mukhtasar), which this book (al-Lubab) is a commentary upon. His full name and death date (428 AH) are given, along with honorifics emphasizing his expertise in both fiqh and hadith. The phrase 'r-rahma' is a supplication for mercy. This section typically provides background on the scholar's life, teachers, students, and works, though the text here only gives the title and brief identification.

Key Terms
ترجمة (tarjamah): A biography or biographical account, often including dates and scholarly achievements.
الإمام الفقيه المحدث (al-imam al-faqih al-muhaddith): Honorific titles indicating the person is a leading authority (imam), a jurist (faqih), and a hadith scholar (muhaddith).

Biography of Imam al-Quduri: A Hanafi Matn Author
Biographical sketch of Imam al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical facts of Imam al-Quduri and explain why his Mukhtasar is foundational in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Imam al-Quduri, a Baghdadi Hanafi jurist, authored Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a primary matn for Hanafi fiqh.

This lesson introduces Imam al-Quduri, the author of one of the earliest and most authoritative Hanafi legal texts. Knowing his biography helps us appreciate the scholarly chain and authority behind the matn we study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and kunyah
Read the Arabic passage and extract the complete name and honorific.
Al-Quduri's kunyah is Abu al-Husayn, even though he may not have had a son named al-Husayn.
2
Note the nisbah and its meaning
Understand that 'al-Quduri' comes from qudur (pots), indicating a family trade in pottery.
Nisbah often indicates profession or place of origin.
3
Memorize birth and death years
Born 362 AH, died 428 AH. He lived 66 years.
These dates place him in the 4th-5th centuries AH.
4
Trace his burial and relocation
Initially buried in his house in Darb Abi Khalaf, later moved to a tomb beside Imam al-Khwarizmi.
His burial next to a Hanafi scholar emphasizes his status.
5
Summarize his life's dedication
The text notes he spent his 66 years in beneficial knowledge, righteous action, and public benefit.
This epitaph reflects the ideal of a scholar in Islam.

Chapter One: Biography of Imam al-Quduri
Section One
Imam al-Quduri: Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad
His name:
Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Ja'far ibn Hamdan al-Quduri al-Baghdadi. He was born in the year 362 AH, and died in Baghdad on Sunday, the fifth of Rajab, and it was said: in the middle of it, in the year 428 AH, at the age of sixty-six years.
He was buried, may Allah have mercy on him, on the day of his death in his house in Darb Abi Khalaf. This was transmitted by al-Khatib and al-Sam'ani, and related by a group including Ibn Khallikan, who added: then he was moved to a tomb in the street of al-Mansur, and buried there next to Imam Abu Bakr al-Khwarizmi Muhammad ibn Musa, the Hanafi jurist and student of Abu Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi, who died in the year 403 AH. Thus al-Quduri lived sixty-six years, spending them in beneficial knowledge, righteous action, and private and public benefit.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to Imam al-Quduri, the author of the famous Hanafi legal text Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It states his full name: Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Ja'far ibn Hamdan al-Quduri al-Baghdadi. The nisbah 'al-Quduri' refers to a profession related to pottery (al-qudur meaning pots), indicating that he or his family were potters. He was born in 362 AH (972-973 CE) and died in Baghdad in 428 AH (1036-1037 CE) at the age of sixty-six. The details of his burial: initially in his house in Darb Abi Khalaf, later moved to a grave next to Imam Abu Bakr al-Khwarizmi, a Hanafi scholar and student of al-Jassas. Al-Quduri's life was dedicated to beneficial knowledge and righteous action, benefiting both individuals and the community. This brief biography situates him within the Hanafi scholarly tradition, linking him to earlier Hanafi authorities.

Key Terms
القدوري (al-Quduri): Nisbah indicating a potter (from al-qudur, pots); the author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi legal text.
أبو الحسين (Abu al-Husayn): Honorific (kunyah) meaning 'father of al-Husayn', even if he had no son named al-Husayn.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The abridged legal manual authored by al-Quduri, widely studied in Hanafi circles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

The Life of Imam al-Quduri: Author of the Hanafi Primer
Biographical sketch of Imam al-Quduri's life and scholarly context.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the full name, birth and death years, and the reason for the title 'al-Quduri', and explain the significance of his Mukhtasar in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Imam al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, written for his son, became the cornerstone of Hanafi fiqh study.

Before studying any text, understanding its author builds trust in its content. Imam al-Quduri was a master jurist who lived in Baghdad's golden age of scholarship. His Mukhtasar, though concise, carries the weight of the Hanafi tradition. This lesson introduces his life, lineage, and the scholarly environment that produced this enduring work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and lineage
Find the complete name as given in the text: Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Ja'far ibn Hamdan al-Quduri al-Baghdadi. Note the order of names and the connection to Baghdad.
The name includes lineage up to his great-great-grandfather.
2
Determine his birth and death dates and place
Locate the years 362 AH for birth and 428 AH for death. Also note the day and month (Sunday, 5th or mid-Rajab) and place (Baghdad).
He lived 66 years.
3
Analyze the origin of his nickname
The text gives two possibilities: relative to a place called Qudur (village or locality near Baghdad) or from selling/making pots (qudur). Understanding this highlights how scholars were sometimes named after their trade or origin.
Both are valid linguistic derivations.
4
Describe his family and scholarly upbringing
His father was a scholar and hadith narrator. Al-Quduri grew up in a household of knowledge and virtue. He excelled in fiqh and hadith.
His father's influence was key.
5
Recognize the motivation behind his Mukhtasar
The text states he compiled the Mukhtasar for his son Muhammad. This personal motivation shows the text was initially a teaching tool for his own family, which later became a standard curriculum book.
His son died young, but the work endured.

Chapter One: Biography of Imam al-Quduri
Section One
Imam al-Quduri Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad
285
His name:
Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad Ahmad ibn ibn Ja'far ibn Hamdan al-Quduri al-Baghdadi. He was born in the year 362 AH, and died in Baghdad on Sunday, the fifth of Rajab, and it is said: in the middle of it, in the year 428 AH, at the age of sixty-six years.
He was buried, may Allah have mercy on him, on the same day he died in his house in Darb Abi Khalaf, as narrated by al-Khatib and al-Sam'ani, and a group including Ibn Khallikan related it, adding: then he was transferred to a burial ground in al-Mansur Street, and buried there next to Imam Abu Bakr al-Khawarizmi Muhammad ibn Musa, the Hanafi jurist student of Abu Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi, who died in the year 403 AH. Thus al-Quduri lived sixty-six years spent in beneficial knowledge, righteous deeds, and private and public benefit.
(1) See al-Jawahir al-Madiyya 1/249.
(2) Wafayat al-A'yan 1/79.

286
Chapter One: Biography of Imam al-Quduri
He became famous by the title al-Quduri, either relative to 'Qudur': a village near Baghdad or a locality in Baghdad, or from selling or making pots (qudur: plural of qidr), either because he engaged in that craft or one of his ancestors did, so they were attributed to it.
Imam al-Quduri grew up in a household of knowledge, virtue, religion, and righteousness. His father, Shaykh Muhammad ibn Ahmad, was a scholar and hadith narrator.
Thus al-Quduri was raised under the care of his father, advancing in knowledge and rank, and the sun of his sciences shone in numerous fields, especially in fiqh and hadith.
As for al-Quduri's offspring, Allah blessed him with a son named Muhammad Abu Bakr, who heard hadith from Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ahmad ibn Shadhan and al-Qadi Abu al-Qasim al-Tanukhi and others, and died in 440 AH young before the time of narration, and it is said he attained knowledge.
Imam al-Quduri compiled his famous Mukhtasar in fiqh for this son. As for Baghdad in the time of Imam al-Quduri, from the mid-fourth century to the third of the fifth century, it was teeming with strong and active scholarly movement, manifested in the spread of schools and well-stocked libraries, holding scholarly circles and brilliant debates, and the abundance of leading scholars in various arts. Undoubtedly, this scholarly environment rich with knowledge and scholars produces a scholar.
(1) See al-Jawahir al-Madiyya 3/29 and al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p.157.
(2) al-Jawahir al-Madiyya 3/64 (1201), 1/28, al-Tabaqat al-Saniyya (1852).
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of Imam al-Quduri, the author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational text in the Hanafi school. The biography is structured into two sections covering his name, lineage, birth, death, burial, the origin of his title, his family background, his scholarly environment, and his son for whom he wrote his famous Mukhtasar. The passage emphasizes his full name: Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Ja'far ibn Hamdan al-Quduri al-Baghdadi. He was born in 362 AH and died in 428 AH at age 66. His death occurred on a Sunday in Rajab, and he was buried initially in his home and later moved to a burial ground near Imam Abu Bakr al-Khawarizmi, a fellow Hanafi. The nickname 'al-Quduri' is explained as either from a location or from selling/making pots. His father was a scholar and hadith narrator. Baghdad during his time was a vibrant scholarly center with many schools, libraries, and scholars. He compiled his Mukhtasar for his son Muhammad, who died young. This biography helps students understand the author's authority and the environment that shaped his work.

Key Terms
القدوري (al-Quduri): Title of Imam Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad, author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Possibly derived from a place or from making/selling pots.
المختصر (al-Mukhtasar): The concise fiqh manual compiled by Imam al-Quduri for his son, became a key Hanafi primer.
