Imam al-Quduri: His Life and Teachers
Biographical overview of Imam al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical details of Imam al-Quduri, including his nickname, upbringing, teachers, and the purpose of his Mukhtasar.

Core Idea
Imam al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, compiled for his son, became the cornerstone of Hanafi fiqh study.

This lesson introduces the life of Imam al-Quduri, the author of the foundational Hanafi text Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Understanding his background, his scholarly environment, and his motivations for writing helps us appreciate the authority and approach of his work. We will explore his nickname, his family, his education, and one of his key teachers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the origin of the nickname 'al-Quduri'
Read the first paragraph to find the two possible derivations: either from a village or quarter called Qudur, or from the trade of selling or making pots (qudur). Note that such nicknames often indicate a scholar's birthplace or profession.
2
Describe his family background
Note that his father was a scholar and muhaddith, and that al-Quduri was raised in a pious household. Also note that his son Muhammad was the intended audience for his Mukhtasar.
The Mukhtasar was written for his son, showing a personal motivation.
3
Summarize his scholarly environment
Baghdad in the 4th-5th centuries AH was a vibrant center of learning with schools, libraries, and debates. This context helped produce a scholar of al-Quduri's stature.
4
Note his late start in learning
According to al-Sakhawi, al-Quduri began serious study later in life, yet he excelled. This refutes the idea that learning must begin in childhood.
This is a noteworthy biographical detail; it shows that dedication can overcome a late start.
5
Name one of his teachers
The text mentions Abu al-Husayn Ubaydullah al-Hawshabi, a reliable hadith scholar. Al-Quduri learned hadith from him, establishing his chain of transmission.
Only one teacher is listed; others are not detailed.

الفصل الأول : ترجمة الإمام القدوري

وقد اشتهر بلقب القدوري، إما نسبةً إلى: «قدور»: قرية قريبة من بغداد، أو محلة في بغداد، وإما نسبة لبيع القدور : جمع : قدر، أو صنعها، وذلك إما لاشتغاله بتلك الصنعة، أو اشتغال أحد آبائه بها ، فنسبوا إليها.

وقد نشأ الإمام القدوري في بيت علم وفضل ودين وصلاح، فكان أبوه الشيخ محمد بن أحمد عالماً ومحدثاً (۱).

وهكذا تربى القدوري في كنف والده، وترقى علماً وقدراً ، وأشرقت شمس علومه في فنون عديدة، وبخاصة في الفقه والحديث.

أما عن ذرية القدوري، فقد رزقه الله ولداً اسمه محمد أبـو الحديث من أبي علي الحسن بن أحمـد بـن شـاذان، بكر، سمع والقاضي أبي القاسم التنوخي وغيرهما ومات سنة ٤٤٠ هـ شاباً قبل أوان الرواية، وقيل: أدرك الدراية (۲).

وقد جمع الإمام القدوري مختصره المشهور في الفقه لابنه هذا. وعن بغداد في زمن الإمام القدوري من منتصف القرن الرابع وثلث القرن الخامس، فكانت تموج بحركة علمية قوية نشطة، تمثلت مظاهرها في انتشار المدارس والمكتبات الحافلة، وانعقاد الحلقات العلمية، والمناظرات الذهبية، وكثرة الأئمة الأعلام في شتى الفنون ولا شك أن هذا الجو العلمي الزاخر بالعلم والعلماء يولد عالماً إماماً فَحْلاً مثل الإمام القدوري.

* وقد وقفت على خبر مجمل عن نشأة الإمام القدوري العلمية، وهو ما ذكره الإمام السخاوي (ت ٩٠٢هـ)، عند حديث: العلم في الصغر كالنقش في الحجر»(۲)، حيث قال: «وهذا محمول على الغالب، وإلا فقد اشتغل أفراد، كالقفال، والقدوري، بعد كبرهم ، ففاقوا في علمهم، وراقوا بمنظرهم». اهـ وذكر هذا الخبر أيضاً نقلاً عن السخاوي صاحب «كشف الخفاء (۳)-

شيوخه :

ذكر مترجمو القدوري أهم شيوخه، ولم يدوّنوا إلا عدداً قليلاً منهم، ومن هؤلاء الأعلام الذين تلقى عنهم :

١ - أبو الحسين عبيد الله بن محمد بن أحمد بن أحوى بن العوام ابن حوشب الشيباني، المعروف بالحوشبي، المولود سنة ٢٩٤هـ، والمتوفى سنة ٣٧٥هـ، رحمه الله تعالى. كان إماماً محدثاً ثقة ثبتاً)، وقد أخذ القدوري الحديث عنه،

(۱) في المقاصد الحسنة . ص ٢٩٣ - ٢٩٥ ، برقم (٧٠٥).
(۲) وهو حديث ضعيف، كما ذكر السخاوي.
(۳) ۸۷/۲، برقم (١٧٥٧).
(٤) له ترجمة في تاريخ بغداد ٣٦٢/١٠.
Chapter One: Biography of Imam al-Quduri

He was known by the nickname al-Quduri, either in relation to 'Qudur': a village near Baghdad, or a district in Baghdad, or in relation to selling pots (qudur): plural of qidr (pot), or making them, either because he engaged in that craft, or one of his ancestors did, so they were attributed to it.

Imam al-Quduri grew up in a household of knowledge, virtue, religion, and righteousness. His father, al-Shaykh Muhammad ibn Ahmad, was a scholar and a muhaddith (1).

Thus al-Quduri was raised under the care of his father, advancing in knowledge and status. The sun of his sciences shone in numerous fields, especially in fiqh and hadith.

As for his offspring, Allah blessed him with a son named Muhammad, Abu al-Hadith [or: Abu Bakr?] from Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ahmad ibn Shadhan, who heard from al-Qadi Abu al-Qasim al-Tanukhi and others, and died in 440 AH young before the time of narration, and it was said he attained knowledge (2).

Imam al-Quduri compiled his famous Mukhtasar in fiqh for this son. As for Baghdad during the time of Imam al-Quduri, from the mid-fourth century to the third of the fifth century, it was bustling with a strong, active scholarly movement. Its manifestations included the spread of schools and rich libraries, the holding of scholarly circles and golden debates, and the abundance of leading imams in various arts. There is no doubt that this scholarly environment rich in knowledge and scholars produces a profound imam like Imam al-Quduri.

* I came across a summary report about Imam al-Quduri's scholarly upbringing, mentioned by Imam al-Sakhawi (d. 902 AH) regarding the hadith 'Learning in childhood is like engraving on stone' (2), where he said: 'This is understood in general, but some individuals, such as al-Qaffal and al-Quduri, engaged in learning after their older age, yet they excelled in their knowledge and were admired for their appearance.' End quote. This report is also mentioned by the author of 'Kashf al-Khafa' (3).

His Teachers:

Those who wrote biographies of al-Quduri mentioned his most important teachers, recording only a few of them. Among these notable figures from whom he learned:

1 - Abu al-Husayn Ubaydullah ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Ahwa ibn al-Awwam ibn Hawshab al-Shaybani, known as al-Hawshabi, born in 294 AH and died in 375 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. He was a reliable, trustworthy imam and muhaddith. Al-Quduri learned hadith from him.

(1) In al-Maqasid al-Hasana, pp. 293-295, no. (705).
(2) It is a weak hadith, as al-Sakhawi mentioned.
(3) 2/87, no. (1757).
(4) His biography is in Tarikh Baghdad 10/362.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction (tarjama) from the commentary 'al-Lubab' by al-Maydani on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. It opens the first chapter with the life of Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), the author of the widely-studied Hanafi matn 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri'. The commentary explains his nickname: either from a village or quarter called Qudur near Baghdad, or from the trade in cooking pots (qudur). It highlights his upbringing in a pious scholarly home under his father, a scholar and hadith transmitter. Al-Quduri's expertise spanned many fields, especially fiqh and hadith. The text mentions his son Muhammad, for whom he compiled his famous Mukhtasar, and notes the vibrant scholarly environment of Baghdad in the 4th-5th centuries AH. A report from al-Sakhawi confirms that al-Quduri began his serious studies later in life yet still excelled. The section concludes by listing one of his teachers: al-Hawshabi, a reliable hadith scholar. This biography establishes the credibility and background of the matn author, which is standard in sharh works.

Key Terms
القدوري (al-Quduri): Nickname of Imam Abu al-Hasan Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri, the Hanafi jurist and author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise Hanafi fiqh manual authored by Imam al-Quduri, widely studied in Hanafi curricula.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Quduri was a Hanafi jurist of 4th-5th century Baghdad whose Mukhtasar, written for his son, remains a key text in Hanafi fiqh education.

Imam al-Quduri: His Teachers, Students, and Unlikely Beginning
Biographical introduction to Imam al-Quduri's scholarly life

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key teachers and students of Imam al-Quduri and explain the significance of his late start in acquiring knowledge.

Core Idea
Imam al-Quduri mastered Hanafi fiqh despite starting his studies in adulthood—proof that sincere effort overcomes age constraints.

This biographical passage from al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri introduces us to the life of Imam al-Quduri, the author of the famous matn (text) in Hanafi fiqh. It highlights a remarkable fact: he began his pursuit of knowledge after adulthood. The passage also lists his most important teachers and students, showing his place in the chain of Hanafi scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the unique feature of al-Quduri's education
Note the report from Imam al-Sakhawi that al-Quduri began studying after adulthood, which was unusual but shows exceptional dedication.
This challenges the common assumption that learning must begin in childhood.
2
Identify the three teachers and their specializations
List the three teachers: al-Hushbi (hadith), al-Muaddib (hadith and narrator of al-Quduri's hadith collection), and al-Jurjani al-Hanafi (fiqh).
Al-Jurjani is the main teacher from whom al-Quduri learned Hanafi fiqh.
3
Note the teacher for fiqh specifically
Al-Jurjani al-Hanafi, a student of Imam al-Jassas, was the primary fiqh teacher. He is buried next to Abu Hanifa.
This shows al-Quduri's direct link to the early Hanafi masters.
4
Identify one prominent student
Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, a famous Shafi'i historian and hadith scholar, studied under al-Quduri.
This indicates al-Quduri's influence extended beyond the Hanafi school.
5
Understand the significance of this biography
Al-Quduri's matn (al-Mukhtasar) became a foundational text in Hanafi fiqh. His late start and his teachers/students solidify his place in Hanafi tradition.
The biography helps us appreciate the chain of transmission and the dedication required for scholarly mastery.

Chapter One: Biography of Imam al-Quduri. An imam, a stallion like Imam al-Quduri. I came across a summary report about Imam al-Quduri's academic upbringing, which Imam al-Sakhawi (d. 902 AH) mentioned regarding the hadith: 'Knowledge in youth is like engraving in stone,' where he said: 'This is taken as the general case, otherwise some individuals, like al-Qaffal and al-Quduri, engaged [in study] after their older age, so they excelled in their knowledge and were delightful in their appearance.' He also mentioned this report narrating from al-Sakhawi, the author of Kashf al-Khafa. His teachers: The biographers of al-Quduri mentioned his most important teachers, and they recorded only a few of them. Among these notable figures from whom he received knowledge: 1. Abu al-Husayn Ubayd Allah ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Ahwa ibn al-Awwam ibn Hushayb al-Shaybani, known as al-Hushbi, born 294 AH, died 375 AH. He was a trustworthy imam and hadith scholar. Al-Quduri took hadith from him and narrated from him. 2. Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ali ibn Suwayd al-Muaddib, the imam and hadith scholar, died 381 AH. Al-Quduri took hadith from him and narrated from him, and al-Quduri's hadith collection (juz') is entirely narrated from him. 3. Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Yahya ibn Mahdi al-Jurjani al-Hanafi, resident of Baghdad, from the great imams and jurists of the Hanafis, and he was a student of Imam Abu Bakr al-Razi al-Jassas. Al-Quduri studied fiqh under him. He died 398 AH and was buried next to the grave of Imam Abu Hanifa. His students: Undoubtedly, many studied under al-Quduri, but the biographical books only recorded the most famous and a few of them. Among those who took from him and later became imams: 1. al-Khatib al-Baghdadi Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Baghdadi, the Shafi'i imam, jurist, hadith scholar, hafiz, and famous historian, author of...
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This is a biographical passage from the introduction of al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri, providing the biography of Imam al-Quduri. The author begins by noting a report from al-Sakhawi that al-Quduri, like al-Qaffal, began his studies later in life yet still excelled. Then it lists three of his teachers: al-Hushbi, a hadith scholar; al-Muaddib, from whom al-Quduri's hadith collection is entirely narrated; and al-Jurjani al-Hanafi, the jurist under whom he studied fiqh. Finally, it mentions one famous student: al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, the renowned Shafi'i historian and hadith scholar. The passage emphasizes al-Quduri's position as a bridge between earlier Hanafi authorities and later scholars.

Key Terms
ترجمة (tarjamah): Biography; a written account of a person's life.
شيوخه (shuyūkhuhu): His teachers; the scholars from whom he studied.
تلاميذه (talāmīdhuhu): His students; those who studied under him.

The Students of Imam al-Quduri: A Scholarly Chain
Biographical list of al-Quduri's students

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the students of Imam al-Quduri listed in the text and explain how this biographical list establishes the authority and transmission of the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Al-Quduri's students formed a living chain of knowledge, securing the school's textual tradition.

Imam al-Quduri's Mukhtasar is a cornerstone of Hanafi fiqh, but a text without a reliable chain of teachers is like a well without a rope. This passage from al-Lubab introduces you to the men who carried al-Quduri's legacy forward. By meeting these scholars, you see how the Hanafi school preserved its rulings across generations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Starting Point
Locate the name of the teacher: Imam al-Quduri. This is the central figure whose students are listed.
Al-Quduri died in 428 AH; his Mukhtasar is the matn being commented upon in al-Lubab.
2
List the Named Students
Read through the passage and write down the names of the seven scholars, along with any titles or descriptions given.
Pay attention to the numbering: 1 (unnamed in the excerpt but described), 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7.
3
Note Their Roles and Achievements
For each student, note their profession (faqih, qadi, grammarian), any works they authored (e.g., commentaries), and their death dates if given.
This shows the diverse ways the Hanafi school was served: teaching, judging, writing.
4
Recognize the Chain of Authority
Observe that some students became teachers of the next generation (e.g., al-Damaghani taught Ibn 'Aqil). This chain (sanad) validates the school's rulings.
A strong sanad means reliable transmission from the founder through the generations.
5
Connect to the Text's Purpose
Understand that the commentator al-Maydani includes this biography to affirm the authority of al-Quduri and his students, making the commentary trustworthy.
This is not just a list; it is a claim of authenticity.

الفصل الأول : ترجمة الإمام القدوري

التصانيف الكثيرة، وصاحب تاريخ بغداد، وأحد أعيان الشافعية، المتوفى سنة ٤٦٣هـ (1)

٢ـ أبو نصر أحمد بن محمد بن محمد البغدادي، المعروف بالأقطع ، الإمام الفقيه الحنفي البارع، شارح مختصر القدوري، المتوفى سنة ٤٧٤هـ (2)

عبد الرحمن بن محمد السرخسي، الإمام الفقيه القاضي، العابد الزاهد، وهو ممن تفقه على القدوري ومن تصانيفه : تكملة التجريد للقدوري، المتوفى سنة ٤٣٩هـ (3)

أبو القاسم عبد الواحد بن علي بن برهان العكبري، صاحب التصانيف، وكان فقيهاً حنفياً، تفقه على القدوري، وكان علماً من أعلام العربية والأنساب، المتوفى سنة ٤٥٦هـ (4)

ه أبو عبد الله محمد بن علي بن محمد بن الحسين بـن عبد الملك الدامغاني الكبير، قاضي القضاة الإمام الفقيه الحنفي، من كبار أعيان الحنفية، وقد انتهت إليه رئاسة الحنفية في زمانه، وهو شيخ ابن عقيل الحنبلي، الإمام المشهور. وكان وافر العقل، كامل الفضل، سديد الرأي، عفيفاً نزيهاً، وكان يُنظّر بأبي يوسف القاضي حشمة وجَاهاً وسؤدداً وعقلاً. ومن مصنفاته: شرح مختصر الحاكم في الفقه الحنفي، توفي رحمه الله سنة ٤٧٨هـ.

٦ ـ أبو الحارث محمد بن أبي الفضل محمد السرخسي، الإمام الفقيه الكبير، روي أنه ذكر عند شيخه الإمام القدوري، فقال عنه :
«ما جاء من خراسان وعبر النهر أفقه منه».
وهو من طبقة الدامغاني، ولم تذكر سنة وفاته.

المفضل بن مسعود بن محمد يحيى التنوخي القاضي الفقيه النحوي، تفقه على القدوري، وله عدة مصنفات، منها: أخبار النحويين، ورسالة في وجوب غسل الرّجلين، توفي سنة ٤٢٣هـ.

*****

(۱) له ترجمة في سير أعلام النبلاء ۲۷۰/۱۸ ، وينظر تاريخ بغداد ٣٧٧/٤، فقد ترجم لشيخه القدوري، ونص أنه كتب عنه.
(۲) له ترجمة في الجواهر المضية ،۳۱۱/۱ ، تاج التراجم ص ١٠، الفوائد البهية ص .2.
(۳) له ترجمة في الجواهر المضية ،۳۹۷/۲ ، تاج التراجم ص ١٨٥، هدية العارفين ٥١٦/١.
(٤) الطبقات السنية ٤٠٠/٤ .
Chapter One: Biography of Imam al-Quduri

Numerous works, author of Tarikh Baghdad, and one of the prominent Shafi'is, died in 463 AH.

2. Abu Nasr Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Baghdadi, known as al-Aqta', the outstanding Hanafi jurist, commentator of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, died in 474 AH.

Abd al-Rahman ibn Muhammad al-Sarakhsi, the jurist judge, ascetic worshiper, who studied under al-Quduri; among his works: Takmilat al-Tajrid li al-Quduri, died in 439 AH.

Abu al-Qasim Abd al-Wahid ibn Ali ibn Burhan al-‘Ukbari, author of many works, was a Hanafi jurist, studied under al-Quduri, and was a leading figure in Arabic and genealogy, died in 456 AH.

He is Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Ali ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Abd al-Malik al-Damaghani al-Kabir, Chief Judge, the Hanafi jurist, one of the great Hanafis, and the leadership of the Hanafis reached him in his time. He was the teacher of Ibn ‘Aqil al-Hanbali, the famous imam. He was of sound mind, complete virtue, sound opinion, chaste and noble. He was compared to Abu Yusuf al-Qadi in dignity, prestige, authority, and intellect. Among his works: Sharh Mukhtasar al-Hakim fi al-Fiqh al-Hanafi; he died in 478 AH.

6. Abu al-Harith Muhammad ibn Abi al-Fadl Muhammad al-Sarakhsi, the great jurist. It is narrated that he was mentioned before his teacher Imam al-Quduri, who said about him: "No one has come from Khurasan and Transoxiana more knowledgeable in fiqh than him." He was of the same rank as al-Damaghani, but his year of death is not recorded.

Al-Mufaddal ibn Mas‘ud ibn Muhammad Yahya al-Tanukhi, the judge, jurist, grammarian; studied under al-Quduri and authored several works, including: Akhbar al-Nahwiyyin and a treatise on the obligation of washing the feet. He died in 423 AH.

*****

(1) His biography is in Siyar A‘lam al-Nubala’ 18/270, and see Tarikh Baghdad 4/377, which includes a biography of his teacher al-Quduri and states that he wrote from him.
(2) His biography is in al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya 1/311, Taj al-Tarajim p. 10, al-Fawa’id al-Bahiyya p. 2.
(3) His biography is in al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya 2/397, Taj al-Tarajim p. 185, Hadiyat al-‘Arifin 1/516.
(4) al-Tabaqat al-Saniyya 4/400.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section from the commentary 'al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri' by al-Maydani. It enumerates the students of Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), the author of the matn 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri', a foundational text in Hanafi fiqh. The section lists seven scholars: (1) A Shafi'i scholar (perhaps the author of Tarikh Baghdad, al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, though here described as Shafi'i), (2) Abu Nasr al-Aqta', a Hanafi commentator, (3) Abd al-Rahman al-Sarakhsi, (4) Abu al-Qasim al-‘Ukbari, (5) al-Damaghani, (6) Abu al-Harith al-Sarakhsi, and (7) al-Mufaddal al-Tanukhi. The biographies highlight the transmission of Hanafi learning, showing the direct link between al-Quduri and later scholars. Al-Damaghani is especially noted as a leading Hanafi judge of his time, and al-Quduri's praise of Abu al-Harith al-Sarakhsi underscores the latter's exceptional knowledge. The footnotes provide references for further biographical study. This helps establish the authority and chain of transmission (sanad) of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
القدوري (al-Quduri): Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri, a leading Hanafi jurist of the 5th century AH, author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
الفقيه (al-faqih): A jurist, one learned in Islamic law (fiqh).
الحنفي (al-Hanafi): A follower of the Hanafi school of jurisprudence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following was a student of Imam al-Quduri and authored a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri?
A) Abu al-Harith al-Sarakhsi
B) Abu Nasr al-Aqta'
C) al-Khatib al-Baghdadi
D) al-Damaghani

Key Takeaway
Knowing the students of al-Quduri gives you confidence in the transmission of Hanafi fiqh from one generation to the next.
